description: "Reference for TVM codepage 0 instructions, opcodes, gas, stack effects, and aliases"
mode: "wide"
---
import { TvmInstructionTable } from "/snippets/tvm-instruction-table.jsx"

TON Virtual Machine (TVM) codepage `0` instruction reference with opcodes, gas, stack effects, implementations, and aliases. The dataset is generated from the current [TxTracer specification](https://txtracer.ton.org/spec/) and preserves a small set of legacy TON Docs entries when TxTracer does not expose an equivalent opcode, so existing anchors remain stable.

<TvmInstructionTable />

{/* STATIC_START tvm_instructions */}
<div hidden>
#### `00` NOP

<p>Does nothing.</p><br />
**Category:** Stack Basic (stack_basic)<br />

```fift Fift
NOP
```

#### `0i` XCHG_0I

<p>Interchanges top element with element at index <code>i</code>.</p><br />
**Category:** Stack Basic (stack_basic)<br />

```fift Fift
s[i] XCHG0
```


<p><strong>Aliases</strong>:</p>
<ul>
<li>
<p><code>SWAP</code></p>
<p>Same as <code>s1 XCHG0</code>.</p>
</li>
</ul>

#### `10ij` XCHG_IJ

<p>Interchanges elements at indices <code>i</code> and <code>j</code>.</p><br />
**Category:** Stack Basic (stack_basic)<br />

```fift Fift
s[i] s[j] XCHG
```

#### `11ii` XCHG_0I_LONG

<p>This instruction is equivalent to <code>XCHG&#95;0I</code> except that it operates on a integer value with bigger range.</p><br />
**Category:** Stack Basic (stack_basic)<br />

```fift Fift
s0 [ii] s() XCHG
```

#### `1i` XCHG_1I

<p>Interchanges second element with element at index <code>i</code>.</p><br />
**Category:** Stack Basic (stack_basic)<br />

```fift Fift
s1 s[i] XCHG
```

#### `2i` PUSH

<p>Copy value of <code>s(i)</code> and pushes it onto the stack.</p><br />
**Category:** Stack Basic (stack_basic)<br />

```fift Fift
s[i] PUSH
```


<p><strong>Aliases</strong>:</p>
<ul>
<li>
<p><code>DUP</code></p>
<p>Same as <code>s0 PUSH</code>.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p><code>OVER</code></p>
<p>Same as <code>s1 PUSH</code>.</p>
</li>
</ul>

#### `3i` POP

<p>Removes the top element from the stack and stores it in <code>s(i)</code>. If <code>i</code> equal to 0, POP is effectively a <code>DROP</code>, i.e. the top element is removed from the stack.</p><br />
**Category:** Stack Basic (stack_basic)<br />

```fift Fift
s[i] POP
```


<p><strong>Aliases</strong>:</p>
<ul>
<li>
<p><code>DROP</code></p>
<p>Same as <code>s0 POP</code>, discards the top-of-stack value.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p><code>NIP</code></p>
<p>Same as <code>s1 POP</code>.</p>
</li>
</ul>

#### `4ijk` XCHG3

<p>Performs <code>s2 s(i) XCHG</code>, <code>s1 s(j) XCHG</code>, and finally <code>s(k) XCHG&#95;0I</code>.</p><br />
**Category:** Stack Complex (stack_complex)<br />

```fift Fift
s[i] s[j] s[k] XCHG3
```

#### `50ij` XCHG2

<p>Performs two stack element exchanges in sequence (<code>XCHG&#95;0I s(i)</code>, <code>XCHG&#95;0I s(j)</code>).</p><br />
**Category:** Stack Complex (stack_complex)<br />

```fift Fift
s[i] s[j] XCHG2
```

#### `51ij` XCPU

<p>Exchanges <code>i</code>-th element with top (<code>XCHG&#95;0I s(i)</code>) and pushes <code>j</code>-th element (<code>PUSH s(j)</code>).</p><br />
**Category:** Stack Complex (stack_complex)<br />

```fift Fift
s[i] s[j] XCPU
```

#### `52ij` PUXC

<p>Pushes <code>i</code>-th element, swaps it, and exchanges with <code>j</code>-th element (<code>PUSH s(i)</code>, <code>SWAP</code>, <code>XCHG&#95;0I s(j)</code>).</p><br />
**Category:** Stack Complex (stack_complex)<br />

```fift Fift
s[i] s[j-1] PUXC
```

#### `53ij` PUSH2

<p>Pushes two values from <code>i</code>-th and <code>j</code>-th positions (<code>PUSH s(i)</code>, <code>PUSH s(j+1)</code>).</p><br />
**Category:** Stack Complex (stack_complex)<br />

```fift Fift
s[i] s[j] PUSH2
```

#### `540ijk` XCHG3_ALT

<p>Performs <code>s2 s(i) XCHG</code>, <code>s1 s(j) XCHG</code>, and finally <code>s(k) XCHG&#95;0I</code>. This is a long form of <code>XCHG3</code>.</p><br />
**Category:** Stack Complex (stack_complex)<br />

```fift Fift
s[i] s[j] s[k] XCHG3_l
```

#### `541ijk` XC2PU

<p>Performs a double exchange (<code>s(i) s(j) XCHG2</code>) followed by pushing a value (<code>s(k) PUSH</code>).</p><br />
**Category:** Stack Complex (stack_complex)<br />

```fift Fift
s[i] s[j] s[k] XC2PU
```

#### `542ijk` XCPUXC

<p>Exchanges second with <code>i</code>-th element, then performs PUXC with <code>j</code> and <code>k-1</code> (<code>XCHG&#95;1I s(i)</code>, <code>PUXC s(j) s(k-1)</code>).</p><br />
**Category:** Stack Complex (stack_complex)<br />

```fift Fift
s[i] s[j] s[k-1] XCPUXC
```

#### `543ijk` XCPU2

<p>Exchanges <code>i</code>-th element with top (<code>s(i) XCHG&#95;0I</code>) and pushes two values (<code>s(j) s(k) PUSH2</code>).</p><br />
**Category:** Stack Complex (stack_complex)<br />

```fift Fift
s[i] s[j] s[k] XCPU2
```

#### `544ijk` PUXC2

<p>Pushes <code>i</code>-th element, exchanges with third, then performs XCHG2 with <code>j</code> and <code>k</code> (<code>PUSH s(i)</code>, <code>XCHG&#95;0I s2</code>, <code>XCHG2 s(j) s(k)</code>).</p><br />
**Category:** Stack Complex (stack_complex)<br />

```fift Fift
s[i] s[j-1] s[k-1] PUXC2
```

#### `545ijk` PUXCPU

<p>Performs PUXC with <code>i</code> and <code>j-1</code>, then pushes <code>k</code>-th element (<code>PUXC s(i) s(j-1)</code>, <code>PUSH s(k)</code>).</p><br />
**Category:** Stack Complex (stack_complex)<br />

```fift Fift
s[i] s[j-1] s[k-1] PUXCPU
```

#### `546ijk` PU2XC

<p>Pushes <code>i</code>-th element, swaps it, then performs PUXC with <code>j</code> and <code>k-1</code> (<code>PUSH s(i)</code>, <code>SWAP</code>, <code>PUXC s(j) s(k-1)</code>).</p><br />
**Category:** Stack Complex (stack_complex)<br />

```fift Fift
s[i] s[j-1] s[k-2] PU2XC
```

#### `547ijk` PUSH3

<p>Pushes three values from different stack positions (<code>PUSH s(i)</code>, <code>PUSH2 s(j+1) s(k+1)</code>).</p><br />
**Category:** Stack Complex (stack_complex)<br />

```fift Fift
s[i] s[j] s[k] PUSH3
```

#### `55ij` BLKSWAP

<p>Permutes two blocks <code>s[j+i+1] ... s[j+1]</code> and <code>s(j) ... s0</code>.</p><br />
**Category:** Stack Complex (stack_complex)<br />

```fift Fift
[i+1] [j+1] BLKSWAP
```


<p><strong>Aliases</strong>:</p>
<ul>
<li>
<p><code>ROT2</code></p>
<p>Rotates the three topmost pairs of stack entries.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p><code>ROLL</code></p>
<p>Rotates the top <code>i+1</code> stack entries.
Equivalent to <code>1 [i+1] BLKSWAP</code>.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p><code>ROLLREV</code></p>
<p>Rotates the top <code>i+1</code> stack entries in the other direction.
Equivalent to <code>[i+1] 1 BLKSWAP</code>.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p><code>-ROLL</code></p>
<p>Permutes two blocks of stack elements, moving the top element to a specified position</p>
</li>
<li>
<p><code>2ROT</code></p>
<p>Rotates three pairs of stack elements</p>
</li>
</ul>

#### `56ii` PUSH_LONG

<p>Copy value of <code>s(i)</code> and pushes it onto the stack. This instruction is equivalent to <code>PUSH</code> except that it operates on a integer value with bigger range.</p><br />
**Category:** Stack Complex (stack_complex)<br />

```fift Fift
[ii] s() PUSH
```

#### `57ii` POP_LONG

<p>Removes the top element from the stack and stores it in <code>s(i)</code>. If <code>i</code> equal to 0, <code>POP&#95;LONG</code> is effectively a <code>DROP</code>, i.e. the top element is removed from the stack. This instruction is equivalent to <code>POP</code> except that it operates on a integer value with bigger range.</p><br />
**Category:** Stack Complex (stack_complex)<br />

```fift Fift
[ii] s() POP
```

#### `58` ROT

<p>Rearranges the top three elements. Moves the third element to the top of the stack: <code>1 2 3 -&gt; 2 3 1</code></p><br />
**Category:** Stack Complex (stack_complex)<br />

```fift Fift
ROT
```

#### `59` ROTREV

<p>Rearranges the top three elements. Places the top element below the first two following elements.: <code>1 2 3 -&gt; 3 1 2</code></p><br />
**Category:** Stack Complex (stack_complex)<br />

```fift Fift
ROTREV
-ROT
```


<p><strong>Aliases</strong>:</p>
<ul>
<li><code>-ROT</code></li>
</ul>

#### `5A` SWAP2

<p>Swaps two pairs of stack elements like <code>2 2 BLKSWAP</code> or <code>s3 s2 XCHG2</code>.</p><br />
**Category:** Stack Complex (stack_complex)<br />

```fift Fift
SWAP2
2SWAP
```


<p><strong>Aliases</strong>:</p>
<ul>
<li>
<p><code>2SWAP</code></p>
<p>Current TxTracer name for <code>SWAP2</code>.</p>
</li>
</ul>

#### `5B` DROP2

<p>Removes top two elements from the stack.</p><br />
**Category:** Stack Complex (stack_complex)<br />

```fift Fift
DROP2
2DROP
```


<p><strong>Aliases</strong>:</p>
<ul>
<li>
<p><code>2DROP</code></p>
<p>Current TxTracer name for <code>DROP2</code>.</p>
</li>
</ul>

#### `5C` DUP2

<p>Duplicates top two stack elements.</p><br />
**Category:** Stack Complex (stack_complex)<br />

```fift Fift
DUP2
2DUP
```


<p><strong>Aliases</strong>:</p>
<ul>
<li>
<p><code>2DUP</code></p>
<p>Current TxTracer name for <code>DUP2</code>.</p>
</li>
</ul>

#### `5D` OVER2

<p>Copies third and fourth stack elements to the top.</p><br />
**Category:** Stack Complex (stack_complex)<br />

```fift Fift
OVER2
2OVER
```


<p><strong>Aliases</strong>:</p>
<ul>
<li>
<p><code>2OVER</code></p>
<p>Current TxTracer name for <code>OVER2</code>.</p>
</li>
</ul>

#### `5Eij` REVERSE

<p>Reverses the order of <code>s[j+i+1] ... s(j)</code>.</p><br />
**Category:** Stack Complex (stack_complex)<br />

```fift Fift
[i+2] [j] REVERSE
```

#### `5F0i` BLKDROP

<p>Removes the top <code>i</code> elements from the stack. Equivalent to <code>DROP</code> performed <code>i</code> times.</p><br />
**Category:** Stack Complex (stack_complex)<br />

```fift Fift
[i] BLKDROP
```

#### `5Fij` BLKPUSH

<p>Performs <code>PUSH s(j)</code> <code>i</code> times.</p><br />
**Category:** Stack Complex (stack_complex)<br />

```fift Fift
[i] [j] BLKPUSH
```

#### `60` PICK

<p>Pops integer <code>i</code> from the stack, then performs <code>s(i) PUSH</code>.</p><br />
**Category:** Stack Complex (stack_complex)<br />

```fift Fift
PICK
PUSHX
```


<p><strong>Aliases</strong>:</p>
<ul>
<li><code>PUSHX</code></li>
</ul>

#### `61` ROLLX

<p>Takes integer <code>x</code> from the top of the stack and moves the <code>x</code>-th element from the top to the top of the stack. For example, <code>ROLL 2</code> is equivalent to <code>ROT</code> (<code>1 2 3 -&gt; 2 3 1</code>).</p><br />
**Category:** Stack Complex (stack_complex)<br />

```fift Fift
ROLLX
```

#### `62` -ROLLX

<p>Takes integer <code>x</code> from the top of the stack and moves the top element to position <code>x</code> from the top. For example, <code>ROLLREV 2</code> is equivalent to <code>ROTREV</code> (<code>1 2 3 -&gt; 3 1 2</code>).</p><br />
**Category:** Stack Complex (stack_complex)<br />

```fift Fift
-ROLLX
ROLLREVX
```

#### `63` BLKSWX

<p>Pops integers <code>i</code>,<code>j</code> from the stack, then performs <code>[i] [j] BLKSWAP</code>.</p><br />
**Category:** Stack Complex (stack_complex)<br />

```fift Fift
BLKSWX
```

#### `64` REVX

<p>Pops integers <code>i</code>,<code>j</code> from the stack, then performs <code>[i] [j] REVERSE</code>.</p><br />
**Category:** Stack Complex (stack_complex)<br />

```fift Fift
REVX
```

#### `65` DROPX

<p>Pops integer <code>i</code> from the stack, then performs <code>[i] BLKDROP</code>.</p><br />
**Category:** Stack Complex (stack_complex)<br />

```fift Fift
DROPX
```

#### `66` TUCK

<p>Copies the top stack item below the second item. For example, <code>1 2 -&gt; 2 1 2</code>.</p><br />
**Category:** Stack Complex (stack_complex)<br />

```fift Fift
TUCK
```

#### `67` XCHGX

<p>Pops integer <code>i</code> from the stack, then performs <code>s(i) XCHG</code>.</p><br />
**Category:** Stack Complex (stack_complex)<br />

```fift Fift
XCHGX
```

#### `68` DEPTH

<p>Pushes the current depth of the stack.</p><br />
**Category:** Stack Complex (stack_complex)<br />

```fift Fift
DEPTH
```

#### `69` CHKDEPTH

<p>Pops integer <code>i</code> from the stack and checks whether there are at least <code>i</code> elements, generating a stack underflow exception otherwise.</p><br />
**Category:** Stack Complex (stack_complex)<br />

```fift Fift
CHKDEPTH
```

#### `6A` ONLYTOPX

<p>Pops integer <code>i</code> from the stack, then removes all but the top <code>i</code> elements.</p><br />
**Category:** Stack Complex (stack_complex)<br />

```fift Fift
ONLYTOPX
```

#### `6B` ONLYX

<p>Pops integer <code>i</code> from the stack, then leaves only the bottom <code>i</code> elements.</p><br />
**Category:** Stack Complex (stack_complex)<br />

```fift Fift
ONLYX
```

#### `6Cij` BLKDROP2

<p>Drops <code>i</code> stack elements under the top <code>j</code> elements.</p><br />
**Category:** Stack Complex (stack_complex)<br />

```fift Fift
[i] [j] BLKDROP2
```

#### `6D` NULL

<p>Pushes a <code>null</code>.</p><br />
**Category:** Tuple (tuple)<br />

```fift Fift
NULL
PUSHNULL
```


<p><strong>Aliases</strong>:</p>
<ul>
<li>
<p><code>NEWDICT</code></p>
<p>Returns a new empty dictionary.
It is an alternative mnemonics for <code>PUSHNULL</code>.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p><code>PUSHNULL</code></p>
<p>Current TxTracer name for <code>NULL</code>.</p>
</li>
</ul>

#### `6E` ISNULL

<p>Pops an element from the stack and checks whether it is a <em>Null</em>, pushing <code>-1</code> or <code>0</code> accordingly.</p><br />
**Category:** Tuple (tuple)<br />

```fift Fift
ISNULL
```


<p><strong>Aliases</strong>:</p>
<ul>
<li>
<p><code>DICTEMPTY</code></p>
<p>Checks whether dictionary <code>D</code> is empty, and returns <code>-1</code> or <code>0</code> accordingly.
It is an alternative mnemonics for <code>ISNULL</code>.</p>
</li>
</ul>

#### `6F0n` TUPLE

<p>Creates a new <em>Tuple</em> from the first <code>n</code> values from the stack.</p><br />
**Category:** Tuple (tuple)<br />

```fift Fift
[n] TUPLE
```


<p><strong>Aliases</strong>:</p>
<ul>
<li>
<p><code>NIL</code></p>
<p>Pushes the only <em>Tuple</em> <code>t=()</code> of length zero.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p><code>SINGLE</code></p>
<p>Creates a singleton <code>t:=(x)</code>, i.e., a <em>Tuple</em> of length one.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p><code>PAIR</code></p>
<p>Creates pair <code>t:=(x,y)</code>.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p><code>TRIPLE</code></p>
<p>Creates triple <code>t:=(x,y,z)</code>.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p><code>CONS</code></p>
<p>Creates a tuple of two elements (cons cell) from the top two stack values</p>
</li>
</ul>

#### `6F1k` INDEX

<p>Returns the <code>k</code>-th element of a <em>Tuple</em> <code>t</code>.</p><br />
**Category:** Tuple (tuple)<br />

```fift Fift
[k] INDEX
```


<p><strong>Aliases</strong>:</p>
<ul>
<li>
<p><code>FIRST</code></p>
<p>Returns the first element of a <em>Tuple</em>.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p><code>SECOND</code></p>
<p>Returns the second element of a <em>Tuple</em>.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p><code>THIRD</code></p>
<p>Returns the third element of a <em>Tuple</em>.</p>
</li>
</ul>

#### `6F2n` UNTUPLE

<p>Unpacks a <em>Tuple</em> <code>t=(x&#95;1,...,x&#95;n)</code> of length equal to <code>n</code>.</p><br />
**Category:** Tuple (tuple)<br />

```fift Fift
[n] UNTUPLE
```


<p><strong>Aliases</strong>:</p>
<ul>
<li>
<p><code>UNSINGLE</code></p>
<p>Unpacks a singleton <code>t=(x)</code>.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p><code>UNPAIR</code></p>
<p>Unpacks a pair <code>t=(x,y)</code>.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p><code>UNTRIPLE</code></p>
<p>Unpacks a triple <code>t=(x,y,z)</code>.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p><code>UNCONS</code></p>
<p>Unpacks a tuple (cons cell) into its two components</p>
</li>
</ul>

#### `6F3k` UNPACKFIRST

<p>Unpacks first <code>k</code> elements of a <em>Tuple</em> <code>t</code>.</p><br />
**Category:** Tuple (tuple)<br />

```fift Fift
[k] UNPACKFIRST
```


<p><strong>Aliases</strong>:</p>
<ul>
<li>
<p><code>CHKTUPLE</code></p>
<p>Checks whether <code>t</code> is a <em>Tuple</em>. If not, throws a type check exception.</p>
</li>
</ul>

#### `6F4n` EXPLODE

<p>Unpacks a <em>Tuple</em> <code>t=(x&#95;1,...,x&#95;$tuple&#95;len)</code> and returns its <code>length</code>, but only if <code>length &lt;= $tuple&#95;len &lt;= 15</code>.</p><br />
**Category:** Tuple (tuple)<br />

```fift Fift
[n] EXPLODE
```

#### `6F5k` SETINDEX

<p>Sets the <code>i</code>-th component of <em>Tuple</em> <code>t</code> to <code>x</code>.</p><br />
**Category:** Tuple (tuple)<br />

```fift Fift
[k] SETINDEX
```


<p><strong>Aliases</strong>:</p>
<ul>
<li>
<p><code>SETFIRST</code></p>
<p>Sets the first component of <em>Tuple</em> <code>t</code> to <code>x</code> and returns the resulting <em>Tuple</em> <code>t&#x27;</code>.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p><code>SETSECOND</code></p>
<p>Sets the second component of <em>Tuple</em> <code>t</code> to <code>x</code> and returns the resulting <em>Tuple</em> <code>t&#x27;</code>.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p><code>SETTHIRD</code></p>
<p>Sets the third component of <em>Tuple</em> <code>t</code> to <code>x</code> and returns the resulting <em>Tuple</em> <code>t&#x27;</code>.</p>
</li>
</ul>

#### `6F6k` INDEXQ

<p>Returns the <code>i</code>-th element of a <em>Tuple</em> <code>t</code>. If <code>t</code> is <em>Null</em> or <code>i</code> is greater than tuple length, returns a <em>Null</em>.</p><br />
**Category:** Tuple (tuple)<br />

```fift Fift
[k] INDEXQ
```


<p><strong>Aliases</strong>:</p>
<ul>
<li>
<p><code>FIRSTQ</code></p>
<p>Returns the first element of a <em>Tuple</em>.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p><code>SECONDQ</code></p>
<p>Returns the second element of a <em>Tuple</em>.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p><code>THIRDQ</code></p>
<p>Returns the third element of a <em>Tuple</em>.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p><code>CARQ</code></p>
<p>Returns the first element of a tuple if it exists, or null if not or the tuple is null</p>
</li>
<li>
<p><code>CDRQ</code></p>
<p>Returns the second element of a tuple if it exists, or null if not or the tuple is null</p>
</li>
</ul>

#### `6F7k` SETINDEXQ

<p>If <code>|t| &lt;= i</code>, first extends the original <em>Tuple</em> to length <code>n&#x27;=i+1</code> by setting all new components to <em>Null</em>. If the original value of <code>t</code> is <em>Null</em>, treats it as an empty <em>Tuple</em>. If <code>i</code> is <em>Null</em> and either <code>|t| &lt;= i</code> or <code>t</code> is <em>Null</em>, then always returns <code>t&#x27;=t</code> and does not consume tuple creation gas.</p><br />
**Category:** Tuple (tuple)<br />

```fift Fift
[k] SETINDEXQ
```


<p><strong>Aliases</strong>:</p>
<ul>
<li>
<p><code>SETFIRSTQ</code></p>
<p>Sets the first component of <em>Tuple</em> <code>t</code> to <code>x</code> and returns the resulting <em>Tuple</em> <code>t&#x27;</code>.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p><code>SETSECONDQ</code></p>
<p>Sets the second component of <em>Tuple</em> <code>t</code> to <code>x</code> and returns the resulting <em>Tuple</em> <code>t&#x27;</code>.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p><code>SETTHIRDQ</code></p>
<p>Sets the third component of <em>Tuple</em> <code>t</code> to <code>x</code> and returns the resulting <em>Tuple</em> <code>t&#x27;</code>.</p>
</li>
</ul>

#### `6F80` TUPLEVAR

<p>Creates a new <em>Tuple</em> <code>t</code> of length <code>n</code> similarly to <code>TUPLE</code>, but with <code>n</code> taken from the stack.</p><br />
**Category:** Tuple (tuple)<br />

```fift Fift
TUPLEVAR
```

#### `6F81` INDEXVAR

<p>Returns the <code>k</code>-th element of a <em>Tuple</em> <code>t</code>, where <code>k</code> is taken from the stack rather than specified in the instruction.</p><br />
**Category:** Tuple (tuple)<br />

```fift Fift
INDEXVAR
```

#### `6F82` UNTUPLEVAR

<p>Unpacks a <em>Tuple</em> <code>t=(x&#95;1,...,x&#95;n)</code> of length equal to <code>n</code>, where <code>n</code> is taken from the stack rather than specified in the instruction.</p><br />
**Category:** Tuple (tuple)<br />

```fift Fift
UNTUPLEVAR
```

#### `6F83` UNPACKFIRSTVAR

<p>Unpacks first <code>k</code> elements of a <em>Tuple</em> <code>t</code>, where <code>k</code> is taken from the stack rather than specified in the instruction.</p><br />
**Category:** Tuple (tuple)<br />

```fift Fift
UNPACKFIRSTVAR
```

#### `6F84` EXPLODEVAR

<p>Unpacks a <em>Tuple</em> <code>t=(x&#95;1,...,x&#95;m)</code> and returns its length <code>m</code>, but only if <code>m &lt;= n &lt;= 255</code>, where <code>n</code> is taken from the stack rather than specified in the instruction.</p><br />
**Category:** Tuple (tuple)<br />

```fift Fift
EXPLODEVAR
```

#### `6F85` SETINDEXVAR

<p>Sets the <code>i</code>-th component of <em>Tuple</em> <code>t</code> to <code>x</code> taken from the stack.</p><br />
**Category:** Tuple (tuple)<br />

```fift Fift
SETINDEXVAR
```

#### `6F86` INDEXVARQ

<p>Returns the <code>i</code>-th element of a <em>Tuple</em> <code>t</code> with <code>i</code> taken from the stack. If <code>t</code> is <em>Null</em> or <code>i</code> is greater than tuple length, returns a <em>Null</em>.</p><br />
**Category:** Tuple (tuple)<br />

```fift Fift
INDEXVARQ
```

#### `6F87` SETINDEXVARQ

<p>If <code>|t| &lt;= k</code>, first extends the original <em>Tuple</em> to length <code>n&#x27;=k+1</code> by setting all new components to <em>Null</em>. If the original value of <code>t</code> is <em>Null</em>, treats it as an empty <em>Tuple</em>. If <code>x</code> is <em>Null</em> and either <code>|t| &lt;= k</code> or <code>t</code> is <em>Null</em>, then always returns <code>t&#x27;=t</code> and does not consume tuple creation gas.</p><br />
**Category:** Tuple (tuple)<br />

```fift Fift
SETINDEXVARQ
```

#### `6F88` TLEN

<p>Returns the length of a <em>Tuple</em>.</p><br />
**Category:** Tuple (tuple)<br />

```fift Fift
TLEN
```

#### `6F89` QTLEN

<p>Unlike <code>TLEN</code> which throws an exception when <code>t</code> is not a <em>Tuple</em>, this instruction provides a way to safely check if a value is a <em>Tuple</em> and get its length in one operation.</p><br />
**Category:** Tuple (tuple)<br />

```fift Fift
QTLEN
```

#### `6F8A` ISTUPLE

<p>Returns <code>-1</code> (true) or <code>0</code> (false) depending on whether <code>t</code> is a <em>Tuple</em>.</p><br />
**Category:** Tuple (tuple)<br />

```fift Fift
ISTUPLE
```

#### `6F8B` LAST

<p>Returns the last element of a non-empty <em>Tuple</em> <code>t</code>.</p><br />
**Category:** Tuple (tuple)<br />

```fift Fift
LAST
```

#### `6F8C` TPUSH

<p>Appends a value <code>x</code> to a <em>Tuple</em> <code>t=(x&#95;1,...,x&#95;n)</code>, but only if the resulting <em>Tuple</em> <code>t&#x27;=(x&#95;1,...,x&#95;n,x)</code> is of length at most 255.</p><br />
**Category:** Tuple (tuple)<br />

```fift Fift
TPUSH
COMMA
```


<p><strong>Aliases</strong>:</p>
<ul>
<li><code>COMMA</code></li>
</ul>

#### `6F8D` TPOP

<p>Detaches the last element <code>x=x&#95;n</code> from a non-empty <em>Tuple</em> <code>t=(x&#95;1,...,x&#95;n)</code>, and returns both the resulting <em>Tuple</em> <code>t&#x27;=(x&#95;1,...,x&#95;&#123;n-1&#125;)</code> and the original last element <code>x</code>.</p><br />
**Category:** Tuple (tuple)<br />

```fift Fift
TPOP
```

#### `6FA0` NULLSWAPIF

<p>Pushes a <em>Null</em> under the topmost <em>Integer</em> <code>x</code>, but only if <code>x != 0</code>.</p><br />
**Category:** Tuple (tuple)<br />

```fift Fift
NULLSWAPIF
```

#### `6FA1` NULLSWAPIFNOT

<p>Pushes a <em>Null</em> under the topmost <em>Integer</em> <code>x</code>, but only if <code>x == 0</code>. May be used for stack alignment after quiet primitives such as <code>PLDUXQ</code>.</p><br />
**Category:** Tuple (tuple)<br />

```fift Fift
NULLSWAPIFNOT
```

#### `6FA2` NULLROTRIF

<p>Pushes a <em>Null</em> under the second stack entry from the top, but only if the topmost <em>Integer</em> <code>y</code> is non-zero.</p><br />
**Category:** Tuple (tuple)<br />

```fift Fift
NULLROTRIF
```

#### `6FA3` NULLROTRIFNOT

**Category:** Tuple (tuple)<br />

```fift Fift
NULLROTRIFNOT
```

#### `6FA4` NULLSWAPIF2

**Category:** Tuple (tuple)<br />

```fift Fift
NULLSWAPIF2
```

#### `6FA5` NULLSWAPIFNOT2

**Category:** Tuple (tuple)<br />

```fift Fift

```

#### `6FA6` NULLROTRIF2

**Category:** Tuple (tuple)<br />


#### `6FA7` NULLROTRIFNOT2

#### `7i` PUSHINT_4

<p>Pushes tiny signed integer <code>x</code> onto the stack. Note that the instruction does not have the usual 4-bit range for the argument, but <code>-5 &lt;= x &lt;= 10</code>!</p><br />

</ul>

#### `88` PUSHREF

<p>Pushes the reference <code>ref</code> onto the stack.
<em>Details:</em> Pushes the first reference of <code>cc.code</code> onto the stack as a <em>Cell</em> (and removes this reference from the current continuation).</p><br />
**Category:** Const Data (const_data)<br />

```fift Fift
[ref] PUSHREF
```

#### `89` PUSHREFSLICE

<p>Pushes the reference <code>ref</code> onto the stack and converts the pushed cell into a <em>Slice</em>.</p><br />
**Category:** Const Data (const_data)<br />

```fift Fift
[ref] PUSHREFSLICE
```

#### `8A` PUSHREFCONT

<p>Pushes the reference <code>ref</code> onto the stack and converts the pushed cell into a <em>Continuation</em>.</p><br />
**Category:** Const Data (const_data)<br />

```fift Fift
[ref] PUSHREFCONT
```

#### `8Bxsss` PUSHSLICE

<p>Pushes the slice <code>slice</code> onto the stack.
<em>Details:</em> Pushes the (prefix) subslice of <code>cc.code</code> consisting of its first <code>8x+4</code> bits and no references (i.e., essentially a bitstring), where <code>0 &lt;= x &lt;= 15</code>.
A completion tag is assumed, meaning that all trailing zeroes and the last binary one (if present) are removed from this bitstring.
If the original bitstring consists only of zeroes, an empty slice will be pushed.</p><br />
**Category:** Const Data (const_data)<br />

```fift Fift
[slice] PUSHSLICE
[slice] SLICE
```


<p><strong>Aliases</strong>:</p>
<ul>
<li><code>SLICE</code></li>
</ul>

#### `8Crxxssss` PUSHSLICE_REFS

<p>Pushes the <code>slice</code> onto the stack.
<em>Details:</em> Pushes the (prefix) subslice of <code>cc.code</code> consisting of its first <code>1 &lt;= r+1 &lt;= 4</code> references and up to first <code>8xx+1</code> bits of data, with <code>0 &lt;= xx &lt;= 31</code>.
A completion tag is also assumed.</p><br />
**Category:** Const Data (const_data)<br />

```fift Fift
[slice] PUSHSLICE
[slice] SLICE
```

#### `8Drxxsssss` PUSHSLICE_LONG

<p>Pushes the <code>slice</code> onto the stack.
<em>Details:</em> Pushes the subslice of <code>cc.code</code> consisting of <code>0 &lt;= r &lt;= 4</code> references and up to <code>8xx+6</code> bits of data, with <code>0 &lt;= xx &lt;= 127</code>.
A completion tag is assumed.</p><br />
**Category:** Const Data (const_data)<br />

```fift Fift
[slice] PUSHSLICE
[slice] SLICE
```

#### `8F_rxxcccc` PUSHCONT

<p>Fetches a simple ordinary continuation from the current code slice and pushes it onto the stack. The length of the continuation is at most 127 * 8 bits and 3 references.</p><br />
**Category:** Const Data (const_data)<br />

```fift Fift
[builder] PUSHCONT
[builder] CONT
```


<p><strong>Aliases</strong>:</p>
<ul>
<li><code>CONT</code></li>
</ul>

#### `9xccc` PUSHCONT_SHORT

<p>Fetches a simple ordinary continuation from the current code slice and pushes it onto the stack. The length of the continuation is at most 15 * 8 bits.</p><br />
**Category:** Const Data (const_data)<br />

```fift Fift
[builder] PUSHCONT
[builder] CONT
```

#### `B7AAcc` QLSHIFT

<p>Shift the top element of the stack left by <code>c</code> bits. If the operand is <code>NaN</code>, returns <code>NaN</code> instead of throwing an exception.</p><br />
**Category:** Arithm Quiet (arithm_quiet)<br />

```fift Fift
[cc+1] QLSHIFT#
```

#### `B7ABcc` QRSHIFT

<p>Shift the top element of the stack right by <code>c</code> bits. If the operand is <code>NaN</code>, returns <code>NaN</code> instead of throwing an exception.</p><br />

```fift Fift
[cc+1] QRSHIFT#
```

#### `B7AC` QLSHIFT_VAR

<p>Shift the top element of the stack left by a number of bits equal to the second element of the stack. If any of the operands is <code>NaN</code>, returns <code>NaN</code> instead of throwing an exception.</p><br />
**Category:** Arithm Quiet (arithm_quiet)<br />

```fift Fift
QLSHIFT
```

#### `B7AD` QRSHIFT_VAR

```fift Fift

```

#### `B7AE` QPOW2

<p>Pops an integer from the stack, raises 2 to the power of it and pushes the result back onto the stack. If the operand is <code>NaN</code>, returns <code>NaN</code> instead of throwing an exception.</p><br />
**Category:** Arithm Quiet (arithm_quiet)<br />

```fift Fift
QPOW2
```

**Category:** Arithm Quiet (arithm_quiet)<br />

```fift Fift

```


#### `BF` CMP

<p>Computes the sign of <code>x-y</code>:
<code>-1</code> if <code>xy</code>.
No integer overflow can occur here unless <code>x</code> or <code>y</code> is a <code>NaN</code>.</p><br />
**Category:** Compare Int (compare_int)<br />

```fift Fift
CMP
```

#### `C0yy` EQINT

<p>Compares <code>x</code> from stack and <code>y</code> from arguments for equality and returns <code>-1</code> if equal and <code>0</code> otherwise.</p><br />
**Category:** Compare Int (compare_int)<br />

```fift Fift
[yy] EQINT
```

<ul>
<li>

```fift Fift

[yy-1] LEQINT
```

<ul>
<li>

<p>Checks whether an integer is negative. Corresponds to Forth&#x27;s <code>0&lt;</code>.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p><code>ISNPOS</code></p>
<p>Checks whether an integer is non-positive.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p><code>LEQINT</code></p>
<p>Checks if an integer is less than or equal to a given value</p>
</li>
</ul>

#### `CF04` STIXQ

<p>Stores a signed <code>width</code>-bit integer <code>x</code> into <code>b</code>. If there is no space in <code>b</code>, sets <code>b&#x27; = b</code> and <code>f = -1</code>.
If <code>x</code> does not fit into <code>width</code> bits, sets <code>b&#x27; = b</code> and <code>f = 1</code>.
If the operation succeeds, <code>b&#x27;</code> is the new <em>Builder</em> and <code>f=0</code>.</p><br />
**Category:** Cell Build (cell_build)<br />

```fift Fift
STIXQ
```

#### `CF05` STUXQ

<p>Stores an unsigned <code>width</code>-bit integer <code>x</code> into <code>b</code>. This is a quiet version of <code>STUX</code> which means that instead of throwing an exception, it pushes a status flag to the stack: -1 if there is no space in <code>b</code>, 0 if the operation succeeds.</p><br />
**Category:** Cell Build (cell_build)<br />

```fift Fift
STUXQ
```

#### `CF06` STIXRQ

<p>Stores a signed <code>width</code>-bit integer <code>x</code> into <code>b</code>, but with arguments in a different order. #### `CF23` ENDXC

<p>If <code>x != 0</code>, creates a <em>special</em> or <em>exotic</em> cell from <em>Builder</em> <code>b</code>.
The type of the exotic cell must be stored in the first 8 bits of <code>b</code>.
If <code>x == 0</code>, it is equivalent to <code>ENDC</code>. Otherwise some validity checks on the data and references of <code>b</code> are performed before creating the exotic cell.</p><br />
**Category:** Cell Build (cell_build)<br />

```fift Fift
ENDXC
```

**Category:** Cell Build (cell_build)<br />


#### `CF50` BTOS

<p>This instruction is equivalent to <code>ENDC</code>, <code>CTOS</code> without extra gas for intermediate Cell creation.</p><br />
**Category:** Cell Build (cell_build)<br />

```fift Fift
BTOS
```

#### `CFC_xysss` STSLICECONST

<p>Stores a constant subslice <code>sss</code>.
<em>Details:</em> <code>sss</code> consists of <code>0 &lt;= x &lt;= 3</code> references and up to <code>8y+2</code> data bits, with <code>0 &lt;= y &lt;= 7</code>. Completion bit is assumed.
Note that the assembler can replace <code>STSLICECONST</code> with <code>PUSHSLICE</code> <code>STSLICER</code> if the slice is too big.</p><br />
**Category:** Cell Build (cell_build)<br />

```fift Fift
[slice] STSLICECONST
```


<p><strong>Aliases</strong>:</p>
<ul>
<li>
<p><code>STZERO</code></p>
<p>Stores one binary zero.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p><code>STONE</code></p>
<p>Stores one binary one.</p>
</li>
</ul>

#### `D0` CTOS

<p><code>c</code> must be either an ordinary cell, or an exotic cell. If cell is exotic, it is automatically loaded to yield an ordinary cell <code>c&#x27;</code> and converted into a <em>Slice</em> afterwards.</p><br />
**Category:** Cell Parse (cell_parse)<br />

```fift Fift
CTOS
```

#### `D1` ENDS

<p>Removes a <em>Slice</em> <code>s</code> from the stack. Throws an exception if it is not empty.</p><br />
**Category:** Cell Parse (cell_parse)<br />

```fift Fift
ENDS
```

#### `D2cc` LDI

<p>Loads a signed <code>width</code>-bit integer <code>x</code> from <em>Slice</em> <code>s</code> and pushes loaded value on stack along with <em>Slice</em> with remainder data.</p><br />
**Category:** Cell Parse (cell_parse)<br />

```fift Fift
[cc+1] LDI
```

#### `D3cc` LDU

<p>Loads an unsigned <code>width</code>-bit integer <code>x</code> from <em>Slice</em> <code>s</code> and pushes loaded value on stack along with <em>Slice</em> with remainder data.</p><br />
**Category:** Cell Parse (cell_parse)<br />

```fift Fift
[cc+1] LDU
```

#### `D4` LDREF

<p>Loads a cell reference <code>c</code> from <code>s</code> and returns the remainder of <code>s</code> as <code>s&#x27;&#x27;</code>.</p><br />
**Category:** Cell Parse (cell_parse)<br />

```fift Fift
LDREF
```

#### `D5` LDREFRTOS

<p>Loads a cell reference <code>c</code> from <code>s</code>, converts it to <em>Slice</em> and returns that <em>Slice</em> and remainder of <code>s</code> as <code>s&#x27;&#x27;</code>.</p><br />
**Category:** Cell Parse (cell_parse)<br />

```fift Fift
LDREFRTOS
```

#### `D6cc` LDSLICE

<p>Cuts the next <code>count</code> bits of <code>s</code> into a separate <em>Slice</em> <code>loaded</code>.</p><br />
**Category:** Cell Parse (cell_parse)<br />

```fift Fift
[cc+1] LDSLICE
```

#### `D700` LDIX

<p>Loads a signed <code>width</code>-bit integer <code>x</code> from <em>Slice</em> <code>s</code>, and returns the remainder of <code>s</code> as <code>s&#x27;</code>.</p><br />
**Category:** Cell Parse (cell_parse)<br />

```fift Fift
LDIX
```

#### `D701` LDUX

<p>Loads an unsigned <code>width</code>-bit integer <code>x</code> from (the first <code>width</code> bits of) <code>s</code>.</p><br />
**Category:** Cell Parse (cell_parse)<br />

```fift Fift
LDUX
```

#### `D702` PLDIX

<p>Preloads a signed <code>width</code>-bit integer from <em>Slice</em> <code>s</code>.</p><br />
**Category:** Cell Parse (cell_parse)<br />


#### `D726` SDBEGINSX

<p>Checks whether <code>s</code> begins with (the data bits of) <code>search</code>, and removes <code>search</code> from <code>s</code> on success. On failure throws a cell deserialization exception. Primitive <code>SDPFXREV</code> can be considered a quiet version of <code>SDBEGINSX</code>.</p><br />
**Category:** Cell Parse (cell_parse)<br />

```fift Fift
SDBEGINSX
```

#### `D727` SDBEGINSXQ

<p>Checks whether <code>s</code> begins with (the data bits of) <code>search</code>, and removes <code>search</code> from <code>s</code> on success. This is a quiet version of <code>SDBEGINSX</code> which means it pushes a status flag onto the stack: 0 if <code>s</code> does not begin with <code>search</code>, -1 if it does.</p><br />
**Category:** Cell Parse (cell_parse)<br />

```fift Fift
SDBEGINSXQ
```

#### `D72A_xsss` SDBEGINS

<p>Checks whether <code>s</code> begins with constant bitstring <code>search</code> of length <code>8x+3</code> (with continuation bit assumed), where <code>0 &lt;= x &lt;= 127</code>, and removes <code>search</code> from <code>s</code> on success.</p><br />
**Category:** Cell Parse (cell_parse)<br />

```fift Fift
[slice] SDBEGINS
```

#### `D72E_xsss` SDBEGINSQ

<p>Checks whether <code>s</code> begins with constant bitstring <code>search</code> of length <code>8x+3</code> (with continuation bit assumed), where <code>0 &lt;= x &lt;= 127</code>, and removes <code>search</code> from <code>s</code> on success. This is a quiet version of <code>SDBEGINS</code> which means it pushes a status flag onto the stack: 0 if <code>s</code> does not begin with <code>search</code>, -1 if it does.</p><br />

#### `D739` XCTOS

<p>Transforms an ordinary or exotic cell into a <em>Slice</em>, as if it were an ordinary cell. A flag is returned indicating whether <code>c</code> is exotic. If that be the case, its type can later be deserialized from the first eight bits of <code>s</code>.</p><br />
**Category:** Cell Parse (cell_parse)<br />

```fift Fift

```

#### `D73A` XLOAD

<p>Loads an exotic cell <code>c</code> and returns an ordinary cell <code>c&#x27;</code>. If <code>c</code> is already ordinary, does nothing. If <code>c</code> cannot be loaded, throws an exception.</p><br />
**Category:** Cell Parse (cell_parse)<br />

```fift Fift

```

#### `D73B` XLOADQ


```fift Fift

```

#### `DB1p` JMPXARGS

<p><em>Jumps</em> to continuation <code>c</code>, passing only the top <code>p</code> values from the current stack to it, the remainder of the current stack is discarded.</p><br />
**Category:** Cont Basic (cont_basic)<br />

```fift Fift
[p] JMPXARGS
```

#### `DB2r` RETARGS

<p><em>Returns</em> to <code>c0</code>, with <code>r</code> return values taken from the current stack.</p><br />
**Category:** Cont Basic (cont_basic)<br />

```fift Fift
[r] RETARGS
```

#### `DB30` RET

<p><em>Returns</em> to the continuation from <code>c0</code>. The remainder of the current continuation <code>cc</code> is discarded.</p><br />
**Category:** Cont Basic (cont_basic)<br />

```fift Fift
RET
RETTRUE
```


<p><strong>Aliases</strong>:</p>
<ul>
<li><code>RETTRUE</code></li>
</ul>

#### `DB31` RETALT

<p><em>Returns</em> to the continuation from <code>c1</code>. The remainder of the current continuation <code>cc</code> is discarded.</p><br />
**Category:** Cont Basic (cont_basic)<br />

```fift Fift
RETALT
RETFALSE
```


<p><strong>Aliases</strong>:</p>
<ul>
<li><code>RETFALSE</code></li>
</ul>

#### `DB32` BRANCH

<p>Pop <code>cond</code> from the stack and perform a <code>RET</code> or <code>RETALT</code> depending on the value of <code>cond</code> (-1 for <code>RET</code>, 0 for <code>RETALT</code>).</p><br />
**Category:** Cont Basic (cont_basic)<br />

```fift Fift
BRANCH
RETBOOL
```


<p><strong>Aliases</strong>:</p>
<ul>
<li>
<p><code>RETBOOL</code></p>
<p>Current TxTracer name for <code>BRANCH</code>.</p>
</li>
</ul>

#### `DB34` CALLCC

<p><em>Call with current continuation</em>, transfers control to <code>c</code> from the stack, pushing the old value of <code>cc</code> into <code>c</code>&#x27;s stack (instead of discarding it or writing it into new <code>c0</code>).</p><br />
**Category:** Cont Basic (cont_basic)<br />

```fift Fift
CALLCC
```

#### `DB35` JMPXDATA

<p><em>Transfers control</em> to continuation <code>c</code> from the stack, converting the remainder of the current continuation (the old value of <code>cc</code>) into a <em>Slice</em> before pushing it onto the stack of <code>c</code>. Unlike <code>CALLCC</code> which pushes the old continuation as is, this instruction converts it to a <em>Slice</em> first.</p><br />
**Category:** Cont Basic (cont_basic)<br />

```fift Fift
JMPXDATA
```

#### `DB36pr` CALLCCARGS

<p><em>Calls</em> continuation <code>c</code> with <code>p</code> parameters, but unlike <code>CALLXARGS</code> which only passes parameters, this instruction also pushes the old value of the current continuation <code>cc</code> (along with the top <code>p</code> values from the original stack) onto the stack of newly-invoked continuation <code>c</code>, setting <code>cc.nargs</code> to <code>r</code>. This allows the called continuation to later return to the caller with the specified number of return values.</p><br />
**Category:** Cont Basic (cont_basic)<br />

```fift Fift
[p] [r] CALLCCARGS
```

#### `DB38` CALLXVARARGS

<p><em>Calls</em> continuation <code>c</code> with parameters and expected return values, but unlike <code>CALLXARGS</code> which takes these values from the instruction itself, this instruction takes <code>p</code> and <code>r</code> from the stack. Here <code>p</code> represents the number of parameters to pass to the continuation, and <code>r</code> represents the number of expected return values.</p><br />
**Category:** Cont Basic (cont_basic)<br />

```fift Fift
CALLXVARARGS
```

#### `DB39` RETVARARGS

<p><em>Returns</em> to the continuation at <code>c0</code>, but unlike <code>RETARGS</code> which takes the number of return values from the instruction itself, this instruction takes the number of return values <code>r</code> from the stack. The top <code>r</code> values from the current stack are passed as return values to <code>c0</code>.</p><br />
**Category:** Cont Basic (cont_basic)<br />

```fift Fift
RETVARARGS
```

#### `DB3A` JMPXVARARGS

<p><em>Jumps</em> to continuation <code>c</code>, but unlike <code>JMPXARGS</code> which takes the number of parameters from the instruction itself, this instruction takes the number of parameters <code>p</code> from the stack. Only the top <code>p</code> values from the current stack are passed to the continuation, and the remainder of the current stack is discarded. The remainder of the current continuation is also discarded.</p><br />
**Category:** Cont Basic (cont_basic)<br />

```fift Fift
JMPXVARARGS
```

#### `DB3B` CALLCCVARARGS

<p><em>Calls</em> continuation <code>c</code> with parameters and pushes the old value of the current continuation, but unlike <code>CALLCCARGS</code> which takes the number of parameters and return values from the instruction itself, this instruction takes <code>p</code> and <code>r</code> from the stack. The old value of the current continuation <code>cc</code> (along with the top <code>p</code> values from the original stack) is pushed onto the stack of the newly-invoked continuation <code>c</code>, setting <code>cc.nargs</code> to <code>r</code>. This allows the called continuation to later return to the caller with the specified number of return values.</p><br />
**Category:** Cont Basic (cont_basic)<br />

```fift Fift
CALLCCVARARGS
```

#### `DB3C` CALLREF

<p>Calls the continuation stored in cell reference <code>ref</code>.</p><br />
**Category:** Cont Basic (cont_basic)<br />

```fift Fift
[ref] CALLREF
```

#### `DB3D` JMPREF

<p>Jumps to the continuation stored in cell reference <code>ref</code>.</p><br />
**Category:** Cont Basic (cont_basic)<br />

```fift Fift
[ref] JMPREF
```

#### `DB3E` JMPREFDATA

<p>Jumps to the continuation stored in cell reference <code>ref</code>, converting the remainder of the current continuation into a <em>Slice</em> before pushing it onto the stack of <code>ref</code>.</p><br />
**Category:** Cont Basic (cont_basic)<br />

```fift Fift
[ref] JMPREFDATA
```

#### `DB3F` RETDATA

<p>Returns to the continuation at <code>c0</code>, converting the remainder of the current continuation into a <em>Slice</em> and pushing it onto the stack of <code>c0</code>.</p><br />
**Category:** Cont Basic (cont_basic)<br />

```fift Fift
RETDATA
```

#### `DB4fff` RUNVM

<p>Flags:</p>
<ul>
<li><strong>+1</strong> — same_c3 (set c3 to code)</li>
<li><strong>+2</strong> — push_0 (push an implicit 0 before running the code); only works with +1 enabled</li>
<li><strong>+4</strong> — load c4 (persistent data) from stack and return its final value</li>
<li><strong>+8</strong> — load gas limit from stack and return consumed gas</li>
<li><strong>+16</strong> — load c7 (smart-contract context)</li>
<li><strong>+32</strong> — return c5 (actions)</li>
<li><strong>+64</strong> — pop hard gas limit (enabled by ACCEPT) from stack as well</li>
<li><strong>+128</strong> — isolated gas consumption (separate set of visited cells, reset chksgn counter)</li>
<li><strong>+256</strong> — pop number N, return exactly N values from stack (only if res=0 or 1; if not enough then res=stk_und)</li>
</ul><br />
**Category:** Cont Basic (cont_basic)<br />

```fift Fift
flags RUNVM
```

#### `DB50` RUNVMX

<p>Flags:</p>
<ul>
<li><strong>+1</strong> — same_c3 (set c3 to code)</li>
<li><strong>+2</strong> — push_0 (push an implicit 0 before running the code); only works with +1 enabled</li>
<li><strong>+4</strong> — load c4 (persistent data) from stack and return its final value</li>
<li><strong>+8</strong> — load gas limit from stack and return consumed gas</li>
<li><strong>+16</strong> — load c7 (smart-contract context)</li>
<li><strong>+32</strong> — return c5 (actions)</li>
<li><strong>+64</strong> — pop hard gas limit (enabled by ACCEPT) from stack as well</li>
<li><strong>+128</strong> — isolated gas consumption (separate set of visited cells, reset chksgn counter)</li>
<li><strong>+256</strong> — pop number N, return exactly N values from stack (only if res=0 or 1; if not enough then res=stk_und)</li>
</ul><br />
**Category:** Cont Basic (cont_basic)<br />

```fift Fift
RUNVMX
```

#### `DC` IFRET

<p>If condition is met, performs <code>RET</code> which ends the current continuation and returns to continuation in <code>c0</code>. If <code>c0</code> holds the initial <code>quit</code> continuation (that is, the current execution is in the root continuation), the program exits with code 0.</p><br />
**Category:** Cont Conditional (cont_conditional)<br />

```fift Fift
IFRET
IFNOT:
```

#### `DD` IFNOTRET

<p>If condition is met, performs <code>RET</code> which ends the current continuation and returns to continuation in <code>c0</code>. If <code>c0</code> holds the initial <code>quit</code> continuation (that is, the current execution is in the root continuation), the program exits with code 0.</p><br />
**Category:** Cont Conditional (cont_conditional)<br />

```fift Fift
IFNOTRET
IF:
```

#### `DE` IF

<p>If condition is met, performs <code>EXECUTE</code> on <code>body</code> continuation. After the body is executed, execution will return to the next instruction after the <code>IF</code>.</p><br />
**Category:** Cont Conditional (cont_conditional)<br />

```fift Fift
IF
```

#### `DF` IFNOT

<p>If condition is met, performs <code>EXECUTE</code> on <code>body</code> continuation. After the body is executed, execution will return to the next instruction after the <code>IFNOT</code>.</p><br />
**Category:** Cont Conditional (cont_conditional)<br />

```fift Fift
IFNOT
```

#### `E0` IFJMP

<p>If condition is met, performs <code>JMPX</code> on <code>body</code> continuation. The remainder of the current continuation is discarded which means that after <code>body</code> completes, control will not return to instruction immediately following the <code>IFJMP</code>. Instead, it will return to the instruction immediately following the instruction that started current continuation. If this continuation is default <code>quit</code>, the program will exit with code 0.</p><br />
**Category:** Cont Conditional (cont_conditional)<br />

```fift Fift
IFJMP
```

#### `E1` IFNOTJMP

<p>If condition is met, performs <code>JMPX</code> on <code>body</code> continuation. The remainder of the current continuation is discarded which means that after <code>body</code> completes, control will not return to instruction immediately following the <code>IFNOTJMP</code>. Instead, it will return to the instruction immediately following the instruction that started current continuation. If this continuation is default <code>quit</code>, the program will exit with code 0.</p><br />
**Category:** Cont Conditional (cont_conditional)<br />

```fift Fift
IFNOTJMP
```

#### `E2` IFELSE

<p>If condition is met, performs <code>EXECUTE</code> on <code>body</code> continuation, otherwise performs <code>EXECUTE</code> on <code>else</code> continuation. After the either body is executed, execution will return to the next instruction after the <code>IFELSE</code>.</p><br />
**Category:** Cont Conditional (cont_conditional)<br />

```fift Fift
IFELSE
```

#### `E300` IFREF

<p>If condition is met, load reference from the current code cell, transforms it to a <em>Slice</em> and then to an ordinary <em>Continuation</em> and finally transfers execution to it. After the body is executed, execution will return to the next instruction after the <code>IFREF</code>. When condition is not met, reference is not loaded, so instruction does not consume extra gas for cell loading.</p><br />
**Category:** Cont Conditional (cont_conditional)<br />

```fift Fift
[ref] IFREF
```

#### `E301` IFNOTREF

<p>If condition is met, load reference from the current code cell, transforms it to a <em>Slice</em> and then to an ordinary <em>Continuation</em> and finally transfers execution to it. After the body is executed, execution will return to the next instruction after the <code>IFNOTREF</code>. When condition is not met, reference is not loaded, so instruction does not consume extra gas for cell loading.</p><br />
**Category:** Cont Conditional (cont_conditional)<br />

```fift Fift
[ref] IFNOTREF
```

#### `E302` IFJMPREF

<p>If condition is met, load reference from the current code cell, transforms it to a <em>Slice</em> and then to an ordinary <em>Continuation</em> and finally jumps to it. The remainder of the current continuation is discarded which means that after <code>body</code> completes, control will not return to instruction immediately following the <code>IFJMPREF</code>. Instead, it will return to the instruction immediately following the instruction that started current continuation. If this continuation is default <code>quit</code>, the program will exit with code 0. When condition is not met, reference is not loaded, so instruction does not consume extra gas for cell loading.</p><br />
**Category:** Cont Conditional (cont_conditional)<br />

```fift Fift
[ref] IFJMPREF
```

#### `E303` IFNOTJMPREF

<p>If condition is met, load reference from the current code cell, transforms it to a <em>Slice</em> and then to an ordinary <em>Continuation</em> and finally jumps to it. The remainder of the current continuation is discarded which means that after <code>body</code> completes, control will not return to instruction immediately following the <code>IFNOTJMPREF</code>. Instead, it will return to the instruction immediately following the instruction that started current continuation. If this continuation is default <code>quit</code>, the program will exit with code 0. When condition is not met, reference is not loaded, so instruction does not consume extra gas for cell loading.</p><br />
**Category:** Cont Conditional (cont_conditional)<br />

```fift Fift
[ref] IFNOTJMPREF
```

#### `E304` CONDSEL

<p>No type checks are performed on <code>x</code> and <code>y</code>, so this can be thought of as a conditional stack operation.</p><br />
**Category:** Cont Conditional (cont_conditional)<br />

```fift Fift
CONDSEL
```

#### `E305` CONDSELCHK

<p>This instruction checks whether <code>x</code> and <code>y</code> have the same type, unlike <code>CONDSEL</code>.</p><br />
**Category:** Cont Conditional (cont_conditional)<br />

```fift Fift
CONDSELCHK
```

#### `E308` IFRETALT

<p>If condition is met, performs <code>RETALT</code> which ends the current continuation and returns to continuation in <code>c1</code>. If <code>c1</code> holds the initial <code>quit</code> continuation (that is, the current execution is in the root continuation), the program exits with code 0.</p><br />
**Category:** Cont Conditional (cont_conditional)<br />

```fift Fift
IFRETALT
```

#### `E309` IFNOTRETALT

<p>If condition is met, performs <code>RETALT</code> which ends the current continuation and returns to continuation in <code>c1</code>. If <code>c1</code> holds the initial <code>quit</code> continuation (that is, the current execution is in the root continuation), the program exits with code 0.</p><br />
**Category:** Cont Conditional (cont_conditional)<br />

```fift Fift
IFNOTRETALT
```

#### `E30D` IFREFELSE

<p>If condition is met, load reference from the current code cell, transforms it to a <em>Slice</em> and then to an ordinary <em>Continuation</em> and finally transfers execution to it. Otherwise, performs <code>EXECUTE</code> on <code>else</code> continuation. After either body is executed, execution will return to the next instruction after the <code>IFREFELSE</code>. When condition is not met, reference for <code>body</code> is not loaded, so instruction does not consume extra gas for cell loading.</p><br />
**Category:** Cont Conditional (cont_conditional)<br />

```fift Fift
[ref] IFREFELSE
```

#### `E30E` IFELSEREF

<p>If condition is met, performs <code>EXECUTE</code> on <code>body</code> continuation. Otherwise, load reference from the current code cell, transforms it to a <em>Slice</em> and then to an ordinary <em>Continuation</em> and finally transfers execution to it. After either body is executed, execution will return to the next instruction after the <code>IFELSEREF</code>. When condition is met, reference for <code>else</code> is not loaded, so instruction does not consume extra gas for cell loading.</p><br />
**Category:** Cont Conditional (cont_conditional)<br />

```fift Fift
[ref] IFELSEREF
```

#### `E30F` IFREFELSEREF

<p>If condition is met, load first reference from the current code cell, transforms it to a <em>Slice</em> and then to an ordinary <em>Continuation</em> and finally transfers execution to it. Otherwise, load second reference from the current code cell, transforms it to a <em>Slice</em> and then to an ordinary <em>Continuation</em> and finally transfers execution to it. After either body is executed, execution will return to the next instruction after the <code>IFREFELSEREF</code>.</p><br />
**Category:** Cont Conditional (cont_conditional)<br />

```fift Fift
[ref] [ref] IFREFELSEREF
```

#### `E39_n` IFBITJMP

<p>If condition is met, performs <code>JMPX</code> on <code>body</code> continuation. Value <code>x</code> remains on the stack and available in <code>body</code> continuation. The remainder of the current continuation is discarded which means that after <code>body</code> completes, control will not return to instruction immediately following the <code>IFBITJMP</code>. Instead, it will return to the instruction immediately following the instruction that started current continuation. If this continuation is default <code>quit</code>, the program will exit with code 0.</p><br />
**Category:** Cont Conditional (cont_conditional)<br />

```fift Fift
[n] IFBITJMP
```

#### `E3B_n` IFNBITJMP

<p>If condition is met, performs <code>JMPX</code> on <code>body</code> continuation. Value <code>x</code> remains on the stack and available in <code>body</code> continuation. The remainder of the current continuation is discarded which means that after <code>body</code> completes, control will not return to instruction immediately following the <code>IFNBITJMP</code>. Instead, it will return to the instruction immediately following the instruction that started current continuation. If this continuation is default <code>quit</code>, the program will exit with code 0.</p><br />
**Category:** Cont Conditional (cont_conditional)<br />

```fift Fift
[n] IFNBITJMP
```

#### `E3D_n` IFBITJMPREF

<p>If condition is met, load reference from the current code cell, transforms it to a <em>Slice</em> and then to an ordinary <em>Continuation</em> and finally jumps to it. Value <code>x</code> remains on the stack and available in <code>body</code> continuation. The remainder of the current continuation is discarded which means that after <code>body</code> completes, control will not return to instruction immediately following the <code>IFBITJMPREF</code>. Instead, it will return to the instruction immediately following the instruction that started current continuation. If this continuation is default <code>quit</code>, the program will exit with code 0. When condition is not met, reference is not loaded, so instruction does not consume extra gas for cell loading.</p><br />
**Category:** Cont Conditional (cont_conditional)<br />

```fift Fift
[ref] [n] IFBITJMPREF
```

#### `E3F_n` IFNBITJMPREF

<p>If condition is met, load reference from the current code cell, transforms it to a <em>Slice</em> and then to an ordinary <em>Continuation</em> and finally jumps to it. Value <code>x</code> remains on the stack and available in <code>body</code> continuation. The remainder of the current continuation is discarded which means that after <code>body</code> completes, control will not return to instruction immediately following the <code>IFNBITJMPREF</code>. Instead, it will return to the instruction immediately following the instruction that started current continuation. If this continuation is default <code>quit</code>, the program will exit with code 0. When condition is not met, reference is not loaded, so instruction does not consume extra gas for cell loading.</p><br />
**Category:** Cont Conditional (cont_conditional)<br />

```fift Fift
[ref] [n] IFNBITJMPREF
```

#### `E4` REPEAT

<p><code>RET</code> inside the code of <code>body</code> works as a <code>continue</code>, not as a <code>break</code>. To <code>break</code> from the loop, use either alternative loop <code>REPEATBRK</code> + <code>RETALT</code> or <code>RETALT</code>, along with a <code>SETEXITALT</code> before the loop.</p><br />
**Category:** Cont Loops (cont_loops)<br />

```fift Fift
REPEAT
```

#### `E5` REPEATEND

<p>Unlike <code>REPEAT</code> which executes a separate continuation <code>body</code> as the loop body, this instruction uses the current continuation itself as the loop body.</p><br />
**Category:** Cont Loops (cont_loops)<br />

```fift Fift
REPEATEND
REPEAT:
```

#### `E6` UNTIL

<p>The actual implementation of this primitive involves an extraordinary continuation <code>ec&#95;until</code> with its arguments set to the <code>body</code> of the loop and the original current continuation <code>cc</code>. This extraordinary continuation is then saved into the savelist of <code>body</code> as <code>body.c0</code> and the modified <code>body</code> is then executed. The other loop primitives are implemented similarly with the aid of suitable extraordinary continuations.</p><br />
**Category:** Cont Loops (cont_loops)<br />

```fift Fift
UNTIL
```

#### `E7` UNTILEND

<p>Unlike <code>UNTIL</code> which executes a separate continuation as the loop body, this instruction uses the current continuation itself as the loop body. When the loop exit condition is satisfied (when <code>cond</code> is <strong>non-zero</strong>), performs a <code>RET</code>.</p><br />
**Category:** Cont Loops (cont_loops)<br />

```fift Fift
UNTILEND
UNTIL:
```

#### `E8` WHILE

<p>The actual implementation of this primitive involves an extraordinary continuation <code>ec&#95;while</code>.</p><br />
**Category:** Cont Loops (cont_loops)<br />

```fift Fift
WHILE
```

#### `E9` WHILEEND

<p>Unlike <code>WHILE</code> which executes a separate continuation <code>body</code> as the loop body, this instruction uses the current continuation itself as the loop body.</p><br />
**Category:** Cont Loops (cont_loops)<br />

```fift Fift
WHILEEND
```

#### `EA` AGAIN

<p>Unlike <code>REPEAT</code> which executes a continuation a specified number of times, this instruction creates an infinite loop. <code>RET</code> inside <code>body</code> code starts a new iteration of an infinite loop, rather than breaks from the loop. <code>AGAIN</code> loop can be exited only by an exception, <code>RETALT</code> with a <code>SETEXITALT</code> before the loop, or an explicit <code>JMPX</code>. Another way is to use <code>AGAINBRK</code>, which also sets <code>c1</code> to <code>cc</code>, and <code>RETALT</code> in the body, which will transfer control to the original <code>cc</code> and exit the loop.</p><br />
**Category:** Cont Loops (cont_loops)<br />

```fift Fift
AGAIN
```

#### `EB` AGAINEND

<p>Unlike <code>AGAIN</code> which executes a separate continuation in an infinite loop, this instruction uses the current continuation itself as the loop body. <code>RET</code> inside <code>body</code> code starts a new iteration of an infinite loop, rather than breaks from the loop. <code>AGAINEND</code> loop can be exited only by an exception, <code>RETALT</code> with a <code>SETEXITALT</code> before the loop, or an explicit <code>JMPX</code>. Another way is to use <code>AGAINENDBRK</code>, which also sets <code>c1</code> to <code>cc</code>, and <code>RETALT</code> in the body, which will transfer control to the original <code>cc</code> and exit the loop.</p><br />
**Category:** Cont Loops (cont_loops)<br />

```fift Fift
AGAINEND
AGAIN:
```

#### `E314` REPEATBRK

<p>Just like <code>REPEAT</code>, but additionally sets <code>c1</code> to the original <code>c</code> after saving the old value of <code>c1</code> into the savelist of the original <code>c</code>. This modification allows <code>RETALT</code> to be used to break out of the loop body, providing a way to exit the loop before all iterations are completed.</p><br />
**Category:** Cont Loops (cont_loops)<br />

```fift Fift
REPEATBRK
```

#### `E315` REPEATENDBRK

<p>Just like <code>REPEATEND</code>, but additionally sets <code>c1</code> to the original <code>c0</code> after saving the old value of <code>c1</code> into the savelist of the original <code>c0</code>. This modification allows <code>RETALT</code> to be used to break out of the loop body, providing a way to exit the loop before all iterations are completed.</p><br />
**Category:** Cont Loops (cont_loops)<br />

```fift Fift
REPEATENDBRK
```

#### `E316` UNTILBRK

<p>Just like <code>UNTIL</code>, but additionally sets <code>c1</code> to the original continuation after saving the old value of <code>c1</code> into the savelist of the original continuation. This modification allows <code>RETALT</code> to be used to break out of the loop body, providing a way to exit the loop before the exit condition is met.</p><br />
**Category:** Cont Loops (cont_loops)<br />

```fift Fift
UNTILBRK
```

#### `E317` UNTILENDBRK

<p>Just like <code>UNTILEND</code>, but additionally sets <code>c1</code> to the original <code>c0</code> after saving the old value of <code>c1</code> into the savelist of the original <code>c0</code>. This modification allows <code>RETALT</code> to be used to break out of the loop body, providing a way to exit the loop before the exit condition is met.</p><br />
**Category:** Cont Loops (cont_loops)<br />

```fift Fift
UNTILENDBRK
UNTILBRK:
```

#### `E318` WHILEBRK

<p>Just like <code>WHILE</code>, but additionally sets <code>c1</code> to the original continuation after saving the old value of <code>c1</code> into the savelist of the original continuation. This modification allows <code>RETALT</code> to be used to break out of the loop body, providing a way to exit the loop before the condition becomes false.</p><br />
**Category:** Cont Loops (cont_loops)<br />

```fift Fift
WHILEBRK
```

#### `E319` WHILEENDBRK

<p>Just like <code>WHILEEND</code>, but additionally sets <code>c1</code> to the original <code>c0</code> after saving the old value of <code>c1</code> into the savelist of the original <code>c0</code>. This modification allows <code>RETALT</code> to be used to break out of the loop body, providing a way to exit the loop before the condition becomes false.</p><br />
**Category:** Cont Loops (cont_loops)<br />

```fift Fift
WHILEENDBRK
```

#### `E31A` AGAINBRK

<p>This instruction sets <code>c1</code> to the original continuation after saving the old value of <code>c1</code> into the savelist of the original continuation. This modification allows <code>RETALT</code> to be used to break out of the infinite loop, providing a way to exit the loop that would otherwise continue indefinitely.</p><br />
**Category:** Cont Loops (cont_loops)<br />

```fift Fift
AGAINBRK
```

#### `E31B` AGAINENDBRK

<p>Just like <code>AGAINEND</code>, but additionally sets <code>c1</code> to the original <code>c0</code> after saving the old value of <code>c1</code> into the savelist of the original <code>c0</code>. This modification allows <code>RETALT</code> to be used to break out of the infinite loop, providing a way to exit the loop that would otherwise continue indefinitely.</p><br />
**Category:** Cont Loops (cont_loops)<br />

```fift Fift
AGAINENDBRK
AGAINBRK:
```

#### `ECrn` SETCONTARGS_N

<p>Pushes <code>r</code> values <code>x&#95;1...x&#95;r</code> into the stack of (a copy of) the continuation <code>c</code>, starting with <code>x&#95;1</code>. When <code>n</code> is 15 (-1 in Fift notation), does nothing with <code>c.nargs</code>. For other values of <code>n</code>, sets <code>c.nargs</code> to the final size of the stack of <code>c&#x27;</code> plus <code>n</code>. In other words, transforms <code>c</code> into a <em>closure</em> or a <em>partially applied function</em>, with <code>n</code> arguments missing.</p><br />
**Category:** Cont Stack (cont_stack)<br />

```fift Fift
[r] [n] SETCONTARGS
```


<p><strong>Aliases</strong>:</p>
<ul>
<li>
<p><code>SETNUMARGS</code></p>
<p>Sets <code>c.nargs</code> to <code>n</code> plus the current depth of <code>c</code>&#x27;s stack, where <code>0 &lt;= n &lt;= 14</code>. If <code>c.nargs</code> is already set to a non-negative value, does nothing.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p><code>SETCONTARGS</code></p>
<p>Pushes <code>0 &lt;= r &lt;= 15</code> values <code>x&#95;1...x&#95;r</code> into the stack of (a copy of) the continuation <code>c</code>, starting with <code>x&#95;1</code>. If the final depth of <code>c</code>&#x27;s stack turns out to be greater than <code>c.nargs</code>, a stack overflow exception is generated.</p>
</li>
</ul>

#### `ED0p` RETURNARGS

<p>Leaves only the top <code>p</code> values in the current stack (somewhat similarly to <code>ONLYTOPX</code>), with all the unused bottom values not discarded, but saved into continuation <code>c0</code> in the same way as <code>SETCONTARGS</code> does.</p><br />
**Category:** Cont Stack (cont_stack)<br />

```fift Fift
[p] RETURNARGS
```

#### `ED10` RETURNVARARGS

<p>Leaves only the top <code>p</code> values in the current stack, where <code>p</code> is taken from the stack. Unlike <code>RETURNARGS</code> which takes the number of values to keep from the instruction itself, this instruction takes this number from the stack. All the unused bottom values are not discarded, but saved into continuation <code>c0</code> in the same way as <code>SETCONTARGS</code> does.</p><br />
**Category:** Cont Stack (cont_stack)<br />

```fift Fift
RETURNVARARGS
```

#### `ED11` SETCONTVARARGS

<p>Pushes values onto the stack of a continuation and optionally sets the number of missing arguments. Unlike <code>SETCONTARGS</code> which takes the number of values to push and the number of missing arguments from the instruction itself, this instruction takes <code>r</code> and <code>n</code> from the stack. It pushes <code>r</code> values from the current stack onto the stack of continuation <code>c</code>, and for <code>n</code> not equal to -1, sets <code>c.nargs</code> to the final size of the stack of <code>c</code> plus <code>n</code>, effectively creating a closure with <code>n</code> missing arguments.</p><br />
**Category:** Cont Stack (cont_stack)<br />

```fift Fift
SETCONTVARARGS
```

#### `ED12` SETNUMVARARGS

<p>Sets the number of arguments expected by continuation <code>c</code>. If <code>n=-1</code>, this operation does nothing (<code>c&#x27;=c</code>). Otherwise, it sets <code>c.nargs</code> to <code>n</code>, where <code>n</code> is taken from the stack. Unlike <code>SETNUMARGS</code> which takes the number of expected arguments from the instruction itself, this instruction takes this number from the stack.</p><br />
**Category:** Cont Stack (cont_stack)<br />

```fift Fift
SETNUMVARARGS
```

#### `ED1E` BLESS

<p>Transforms a <em>Slice</em> <code>s</code> into a simple ordinary continuation <code>c</code>, with <code>c.code=s</code> and an empty stack and savelist.</p><br />
**Category:** Cont Create (cont_create)<br />

```fift Fift
BLESS
```

#### `ED1F` BLESSVARARGS

<p>Transforms a <em>Slice</em> into a simple ordinary continuation and sets its arguments from the stack.</p><br />
**Category:** Cont Create (cont_create)<br />

```fift Fift
BLESSVARARGS
```

#### `EErn` BLESSARGS

<p>The value of <code>n</code> is represented inside the instruction by the 4-bit integer <code>n mod 16</code>.</p><br />
**Category:** Cont Create (cont_create)<br />

```fift Fift
[r] [n] BLESSARGS
```


<p><strong>Aliases</strong>:</p>
<ul>
<li>
<p><code>BLESSNUMARGS</code></p>
<p>Also transforms a <em>Slice</em> <code>s</code> into a <em>Continuation</em> <code>c</code>, but sets <code>c.nargs</code> to <code>0 &lt;= n &lt;= 14</code>.</p>
</li>
</ul>

#### `ED4i` PUSHCTR

<p>Pushes the current value of control register <code>c(i)</code>. If the control register is not supported in the current codepage, or if it does not have a value, throws an exception.</p><br />
**Category:** Cont Registers (cont_registers)<br />

```fift Fift
c[i] PUSHCTR
c[i] PUSH
```


<p><strong>Aliases</strong>:</p>
<ul>
<li>
<p><code>PUSHROOT</code></p>
<p>Pushes the &#x27;&#x27;global data root&#x27;&#x27; cell reference, thus enabling access to persistent smart-contract data.</p>
</li>
</ul>

#### `ED5i` POPCTR

<p>Pops a value <code>x</code> from the stack and stores it into control register <code>c(i)</code>, if supported in the current codepage. Notice that if a control register accepts only values of a specific type, a type-checking exception may occur.</p><br />
**Category:** Cont Registers (cont_registers)<br />

```fift Fift
c[i] POPCTR
c[i] POP
```


<p><strong>Aliases</strong>:</p>
<ul>
<li>
<p><code>POPROOT</code></p>
<p>Sets the &#x27;&#x27;global data root&#x27;&#x27; cell reference, thus allowing modification of persistent smart-contract data.</p>
</li>
</ul>

#### `ED6i` SETCONTCTR

<p>Stores <code>x</code> into the savelist of continuation <code>c</code> as <code>c(i)</code>, and returns the resulting continuation <code>c&#x27;</code>. Almost all operations with continuations may be expressed in terms of <code>SETCONTCTR</code>, <code>POPCTR</code>, and <code>PUSHCTR</code>.</p><br />
**Category:** Cont Registers (cont_registers)<br />

```fift Fift
c[i] SETCONT
c[i] SETCONTCTR
```


<p><strong>Aliases</strong>:</p>
<ul>
<li><code>SETCONT</code></li>
</ul>

#### `ED7i` SETRETCTR

<p>Stores the value from control register <code>c(i)</code> into the savelist of continuation <code>c0</code>.</p><br />
**Category:** Cont Registers (cont_registers)<br />

```fift Fift
c[i] SETRETCTR
```

#### `ED8i` SETALTCTR

<p>Stores the value from control register <code>c(i)</code> into the savelist of continuation <code>c1</code>.</p><br />
**Category:** Cont Registers (cont_registers)<br />

```fift Fift
c[i] SETALTCTR
```

#### `ED9i` POPSAVE

<p>Pops a value from the stack and stores it into control register <code>c(i)</code>, but also saves the old value of <code>c(i)</code> into continuation <code>c0</code>.</p><br />
**Category:** Cont Registers (cont_registers)<br />

```fift Fift
c[i] POPSAVE
c[i] POPCTRSAVE
```


<p><strong>Aliases</strong>:</p>
<ul>
<li><code>POPCTRSAVE</code></li>
</ul>

#### `EDAi` SAVE

<p>Saves the current value of <code>c(i)</code> into the savelist of continuation <code>c0</code>. If an entry for <code>c(i)</code> is already present in the savelist of <code>c0</code>, nothing is done.</p><br />
**Category:** Cont Registers (cont_registers)<br />

```fift Fift
c[i] SAVE
c[i] SAVECTR
```


<p><strong>Aliases</strong>:</p>
<ul>
<li>
<p><code>SAVECTR</code></p>
<p>Current TxTracer name for <code>SAVE</code>.</p>
</li>
</ul>

#### `EDBi` SAVEALT

<p>Similar to <code>SAVECTR c(i)</code>, but saves the current value of <code>c(i)</code> into the savelist of <code>c1</code>, not <code>c0</code>.</p><br />
**Category:** Cont Registers (cont_registers)<br />

```fift Fift
c[i] SAVEALT
c[i] SAVEALTCTR
```


<p><strong>Aliases</strong>:</p>
<ul>
<li>
<p><code>SAVEALTCTR</code></p>
<p>Current TxTracer name for <code>SAVEALT</code>.</p>
</li>
</ul>

#### `EDCi` SAVEBOTH

<p>Saves the current value of <code>c(i)</code> into the savelist of both <code>c0</code> and <code>c1</code>.</p><br />
**Category:** Cont Registers (cont_registers)<br />

```fift Fift
c[i] SAVEBOTH
c[i] SAVEBOTHCTR
```


<p><strong>Aliases</strong>:</p>
<ul>
<li>
<p><code>SAVEBOTHCTR</code></p>
<p>Current TxTracer name for <code>SAVEBOTH</code>.</p>
</li>
</ul>

#### `EDE0` PUSHCTRX

<p>Pushes the current value of control register <code>c(i)</code> onto the stack, where <code>i</code> is taken from the stack. Unlike <code>c(i) PUSHCTR</code> which takes the register index from the instruction itself, this instruction takes this index from the stack. If the control register is not supported in the current codepage, or if it does not have a value, an exception is triggered.
Notice that this primitive is one of the few &quot;exotic&quot; primitives, which are not polymorphic like stack manipulation primitives, and at the same time do not have well-defined types of parameters and return values, because the type of <code>x</code> depends on <code>i</code>.</p><br />
**Category:** Cont Registers (cont_registers)<br />

```fift Fift
PUSHCTRX
```

#### `EDE1` POPCTRX

<p>Pops a value <code>x</code> from the stack and stores it into control register <code>c(i)</code>, where <code>i</code> is taken from the stack. Unlike <code>c(i) POPCTR</code> which takes the register index from the instruction itself, this instruction takes this index from the stack. If the control register is not supported in the current codepage, or if it only accepts values of a specific type and <code>x</code> is not of that type, an exception is triggered.</p><br />
**Category:** Cont Registers (cont_registers)<br />

```fift Fift
POPCTRX
```

#### `EDE2` SETCONTCTRX

<p>Stores value <code>x</code> into the savelist of continuation <code>c</code> as <code>c(i)</code>, and returns the resulting continuation <code>c&#x27;</code>, where <code>i</code> is taken from the stack. Unlike <code>c(i) SETCONTCTR</code> which takes the register index from the instruction itself, this instruction takes this index from the stack. Almost all operations with continuations may be expressed in terms of this primitive, along with <code>POPCTRX</code> and <code>PUSHCTRX</code>.</p><br />
**Category:** Cont Registers (cont_registers)<br />

```fift Fift
SETCONTCTRX
```

#### `EDE3mm` SETCONTCTRMANY

<p>Takes a <code>mask</code> that describes which control registers of the current continuation should be copied and set in continuation <code>c</code>. Returns the modified continuation. This is similar to <code>SETCONTCTRMANYX</code> but uses fixed <code>mask</code> specified in the instruction.</p><br />
**Category:** Cont Registers (cont_registers)<br />

```fift Fift
SETCONTCTRMANY
SETCONTMANY
```


<p><strong>Aliases</strong>:</p>
<ul>
<li><code>SETCONTMANY</code></li>
</ul>

#### `EDE4` SETCONTCTRMANYX

<p>Takes a <code>mask</code> that describes which control registers of the current continuation should be copied and set in continuation <code>c</code>. This is a more efficient version of multiple <code>SETCONTCTRX</code> calls.</p><br />
**Category:** Cont Registers (cont_registers)<br />

```fift Fift
SETCONTCTRMANYX
SETCONTMANYX
```

#### `EDF0` COMPOS

<p>Computes the composition <code>compose0(c, c&#x27;)</code>, which has the meaning of &quot;perform <code>c</code>, and, if successful, perform <code>c&#x27;</code>&quot; (if <code>c</code> is a boolean circuit) or simply &quot;perform <code>c</code>, then <code>c&#x27;</code>&quot;.</p><br />
**Category:** Cont Registers (cont_registers)<br />

```fift Fift
COMPOS
BOOLAND
```


<p><strong>Aliases</strong>:</p>
<ul>
<li>
<p><code>BOOLAND</code></p>
<p>Current TxTracer name for <code>COMPOS</code>.</p>
</li>
</ul>

#### `EDF1` COMPOSALT

<p>Computes the alternative composition <code>compose1(c, c&#x27;)</code>, which has the meaning of &quot;perform <code>c</code>, and, if not successful, perform <code>c&#x27;</code>&quot; (if <code>c</code> is a boolean circuit).</p><br />
**Category:** Cont Registers (cont_registers)<br />

```fift Fift
COMPOSALT
BOOLOR
```


<p><strong>Aliases</strong>:</p>
<ul>
<li>
<p><code>BOOLOR</code></p>
<p>Current TxTracer name for <code>COMPOSALT</code>.</p>
</li>
</ul>

#### `EDF2` COMPOSBOTH

<p>Computes composition <code>compose1(compose0(c, c&#x27;), c&#x27;)</code>, which has the meaning of &quot;compute boolean circuit <code>c</code>, then compute <code>c&#x27;</code>, regardless of the result of <code>c</code>&quot;.</p><br />
**Category:** Cont Registers (cont_registers)<br />

```fift Fift
COMPOSBOTH
```

#### `EDF3` ATEXIT

<p>Sets <code>c0</code> to <code>compose0(c, c0)</code>. In other words, <code>c</code> will be executed before exiting current continuation.</p><br />
**Category:** Cont Registers (cont_registers)<br />

```fift Fift
ATEXIT
```

#### `EDF4` ATEXITALT

<p>Sets <code>c1</code> to <code>compose1(c, c1)</code>. In other words, <code>c</code> will be executed before exiting current continuation by its alternative return path.</p><br />
**Category:** Cont Registers (cont_registers)<br />

```fift Fift
ATEXITALT
```

#### `EDF5` SETEXITALT

<p>Sets <code>c1</code> to <code>compose1(compose0(c, c0), c1)</code>,
In this way, a subsequent <code>RETALT</code> will first execute <code>c</code>, then transfer control to the original <code>c0</code>. This can be used, for instance, to exit from nested loops.</p><br />
**Category:** Cont Registers (cont_registers)<br />

```fift Fift
SETEXITALT
```

#### `EDF6` THENRET

<p>Computes <code>compose0(c, c0)</code>.</p><br />
**Category:** Cont Registers (cont_registers)<br />

```fift Fift
THENRET
```

#### `EDF7` THENRETALT

<p>Computes <code>compose0(c, c1)</code></p><br />
**Category:** Cont Registers (cont_registers)<br />

```fift Fift
THENRETALT
```

#### `EDF8` INVERT

<p>Interchanges <code>c0</code> and <code>c1</code>.</p><br />
**Category:** Cont Registers (cont_registers)<br />

```fift Fift
INVERT
```

#### `EDF9` BOOLEVAL

<p>Performs <code>cc := compose1(compose0(c, compose0(-1 PUSHINT, cc)), compose0(0 PUSHINT, cc))</code>. If <code>c</code> represents a boolean circuit, the net effect is to evaluate it and push either <code>-1</code> or <code>0</code> onto the stack before continuing.</p><br />
**Category:** Cont Registers (cont_registers)<br />

```fift Fift
BOOLEVAL
```

#### `EDFA` SAMEALT

<p>Sets <code>c1</code> to <code>c0</code>.</p><br />
**Category:** Cont Registers (cont_registers)<br />

```fift Fift
SAMEALT
```

#### `EDFB` SAMEALTSAVE

<p>Sets <code>c1</code> to <code>c0</code>, but first saves the old value of <code>c1</code> into the savelist of <code>c0</code>.</p><br />
**Category:** Cont Registers (cont_registers)<br />

```fift Fift
SAMEALTSAVE
```

#### `F0nn` CALLDICT

<p>Calls the continuation in <code>c3</code>, pushing integer <code>num</code> into its stack as an argument. Essentially it&#x27;s a call to method with <code>num</code> ID in the dictionary.</p><br />
**Category:** Cont Dict (cont_dict)<br />

```fift Fift
[nn] CALL
[nn] CALLDICT
```
