</ul>

#### `F12_n` CALLDICT_LONG

<p>Calls the continuation in <code>c3</code>, pushing integer <code>num</code> with extended range into its stack as an argument. Essentially it&#x27;s a call to method with <code>num</code> ID in the dictionary.</p><br />
**Category:** Cont Dict (cont_dict)<br />

```fift Fift
[n] CALL
[n] CALLDICT
```

#### `F16_n` JMPDICT

<p>Jumps to the continuation in <code>c3</code>, pushing integer <code>num</code> as its argument. Essentially it&#x27;s a jump to method with <code>num</code> ID in the dictionary.</p><br />
**Category:** Cont Dict (cont_dict)<br />

```fift Fift
[n] JMP
```


<p><strong>Aliases</strong>:</p>
<ul>
<li><code>JMP</code></li>
</ul>

#### `F1A_n` PREPAREDICT

<p>This instruction is useful if you want to call continuation with <code>CALLXARGS</code> or <code>CALLCC</code> instead of <code>EXECUTE</code> as <code>CALLDICT</code> does.</p><br />
**Category:** Cont Dict (cont_dict)<br />

[n] PREPARE
[n] PREPAREDICT
```

<li><code>PREPARE</code></li>
</ul>

#### `F22_n` THROW_SHORT

<p>Throws an exception with error code <code>num</code>.</p><br />
**Category:** Exceptions (exceptions)<br />

```fift Fift
[n] THROW
```

#### `F26_n` THROWIF_SHORT

<p>Conditionally throws an exception with error code <code>num</code> if <code>cond</code> is NOT EQUAL to 0.</p><br />
**Category:** Exceptions (exceptions)<br />

```fift Fift
[n] THROWIF
```

#### `F2A_n` THROWIFNOT_SHORT

<p>Conditionally throws an exception with error code <code>num</code> if <code>cond</code> is EQUAL to 0.</p><br />
**Category:** Exceptions (exceptions)<br />

```fift Fift
[n] THROWIFNOT
```

#### `F2C4_n` THROW

<p>Throws an exception with error code <code>num</code>.</p><br />

```fift Fift
[n] THROW
```

#### `F2CC_n` THROWARG

<p>Throws an exception with exit code <code>x</code> taken from the stack.</p><br />

```fift Fift
[n] THROWARG
```

#### `F2D4_n` THROWIF

[n] THROWIF

#### `F2DC_n` THROWARGIF

#### `F2F0` THROWANY

<p>Throws an exception with error code <code>num</code> and parameter set to zero. Parameter represents the additional information passed to the exception handler.</p><br />

```fift Fift
THROWANY
```

#### `F2F1` THROWARGANY

<p>Throws an exception with error code <code>num</code> and parameter set to <code>x</code>. Parameter represents the additional information passed to the exception handler.</p><br />

```fift Fift
THROWARGANY
```

#### `F2F2` THROWANYIF

<p>Throws an exception with error code <code>num</code> and parameter set to zero only if <code>cond</code> is NOT EQUAL to 0. Parameter represents the additional information passed to the exception handler.</p><br />

```fift Fift
THROWANYIF
```

#### `F2F3` THROWARGANYIF

<p>Throws an exception with error code <code>num</code> and parameter set to <code>x</code> taken from the stack only if <code>cond</code> is NOT EQUAL to 0. Parameter represents the additional information passed to the exception handler.</p><br />

THROWARGANYIF

#### `F2F4` THROWANYIFNOT

#### `F2F5` THROWARGANYIFNOT

<p>Throws an exception with error code <code>num</code> and parameter set to <code>x</code> taken from the stack only if <code>cond</code> is EQUAL to 0. Parameter represents the additional information passed to the exception handler.</p><br />
**Category:** Exceptions (exceptions)<br />

```fift Fift
THROWARGANYIFNOT
```

#### `F2FF` TRY

<p>Sets <code>c2</code> to <code>handler</code>, first saving the old value of <code>c2</code> both into the savelist of <code>handler</code> and into the savelist of the current continuation <code>cc</code>, which is stored into <code>body.c0</code> and <code>handler.c0</code>. Then performs <code>EXECUTE</code> on <code>body</code> continuation. If <code>body</code> does not throw any exceptions, the original value of <code>c2</code> is automatically restored on return from <code>body</code>. If an exception occurs, the execution is transferred to <code>handler</code>, but the original value of <code>c2</code> is restored in the process, so that <code>handler</code> can re-throw the exception by <code>THROWANY</code> if it cannot handle it by itself.</p><br />
**Category:** Exceptions (exceptions)<br />

```fift Fift
TRY
```

#### `F3pr` TRYARGS

<p>This instruction is similar to <code>TRY</code>, but with <code>[p] [r] CALLXARGS</code> internally used instead of <code>EXECUTE</code>.
In this way, all but the top <code>p</code> stack elements will be saved into current continuation&#x27;s stack, and then restored upon return from either <code>body</code> or <code>handler</code>, with the top <code>0 &lt;= r &lt;= 15</code> values of the resulting stack of <code>body</code> or <code>handler</code> copied as return values.</p><br />
**Category:** Exceptions (exceptions)<br />

```fift Fift
[p] [r] TRYARGS
```

#### `F400` STDICT

<p>Stores dictionary <code>D</code> into <em>Builder</em> <code>b</code>, returing the resulting <em>Builder</em> <code>b&#x27;</code>.
In other words, if <code>D</code> is a cell, performs <code>STONE</code> and <code>STREF</code>; if <code>D</code> is <em>Null</em>, performs <code>NIP</code> and <code>STZERO</code>.</p><br />
**Category:** Dict Serial (dict_serial)<br />

```fift Fift
STDICT
STOPTREF
```


<p><strong>Aliases</strong>:</p>
<ul>
<li>
<p><code>STOPTREF</code></p>
<p>Stores a dictionary or any cell or null in the builder as an optional reference</p>
</li>
</ul>

#### `F401` SKIPDICT

<p>Loads a dictionary and discards its value.</p><br />
**Category:** Dict Serial (dict_serial)<br />

```fift Fift
SKIPDICT
SKIPOPTREF
```


<p><strong>Aliases</strong>:</p>
<ul>
<li>
<p><code>SKIPOPTREF</code></p>
<p>Skips a dictionary or any cell or null in the slice, used for optional references</p>
</li>
</ul>

#### `F402` LDDICTS

<p>Loads a (<em>Slice</em>-represented) dictionary <code>s&#x27;</code> from <em>Slice</em> <code>s</code>, and returns the remainder of <code>s</code> as <code>s&#x27;</code>.
This is a &#x27;split function&#x27; for all <code>HashmapE(n,X)</code> dictionary types.</p><br />
**Category:** Dict Serial (dict_serial)<br />

```fift Fift
LDDICTS
```

#### `F403` PLDDICTS

<p>Preloads a (<em>Slice</em>-represented) dictionary <code>s&#x27;</code> from <em>Slice</em> <code>s</code>.</p><br />
**Category:** Dict Serial (dict_serial)<br />

```fift Fift
PLDDICTS
```

#### `F404` LDDICT

<p>Loads a dictionary <code>D</code> from <em>Slice</em> <code>s</code>, and returns the remainder of <code>s</code> as <code>s&#x27;</code>. May be applied to dictionaries or to values of arbitrary <code>(^Y)?</code> types.</p><br />
**Category:** Dict Serial (dict_serial)<br />

```fift Fift
LDDICT
LDOPTREF
```


<p><strong>Aliases</strong>:</p>

#### `F406` LDDICTQ

<p>Loads a dictionary <code>D</code> from <em>Slice</em> <code>s</code>, and returns the remainder of <code>s</code> as <code>s&#x27;</code>. May be applied to dictionaries or to values of arbitrary <code>(^Y)?</code> types. This is a quiet version of <code>LDDICT</code> which means that instead of throwing an exception, it pushes a status flag to the stack: 0 if the operation fails, -1 if the operation succeeds.</p><br />
**Category:** Dict Serial (dict_serial)<br />

```fift Fift
LDDICTQ
```

#### `F407` PLDDICTQ

<p>Preloads a dictionary <code>D</code> from <em>Slice</em> <code>s</code>. This is a quiet version of <code>PLDDICT</code> which means that instead of throwing an exception, it pushes a status flag to the stack: 0 if the operation fails, -1 if the operation succeeds.</p><br />
**Category:** Dict Serial (dict_serial)<br />

```fift Fift
PLDDICTQ
```

#### `F40A` DICTGET

<p>Looks up key <code>k</code> (represented by a <em>Slice</em>, the first <code>n</code> data bits of which are used as a key) in dictionary <code>D</code> of type <code>HashmapE(n,X)</code> with <code>n</code>-bit keys.
On success, returns the found value as a <em>Slice</em> <code>x</code>.</p><br />
**Category:** Dict Get (dict_get)<br />

```fift Fift
DICTGET
```

#### `F40B` DICTGETREF

<p>Looks up key <code>k</code> (represented by a <em>Slice</em>, the first <code>n</code> data bits of which are used as a key) in dictionary <code>D</code> of type <code>HashmapE(n,X)</code> with <code>n</code>-bit keys. On success, applies <code>LDREF</code> <code>ENDS</code> to the found value, returning a <em>Cell</em> <code>c</code> instead of a <em>Slice</em>.
This operation is useful for dictionaries of type <code>HashmapE(n,^Y)</code>.</p><br />
**Category:** Dict Get (dict_get)<br />

```fift Fift
DICTGETREF
```

#### `F40C` DICTIGET

<p>Looks up key represented by a signed (big-endian) <code>n</code>-bit <em>Integer</em> <code>i</code> in dictionary <code>D</code> of type <code>HashmapE(n,X)</code> with <code>n</code>-bit keys. On success, returns the found value as a <em>Slice</em> <code>x</code>. If <code>i</code> does not fit into <code>n</code> bits, returns <code>0</code>.</p><br />
**Category:** Dict Get (dict_get)<br />

```fift Fift
DICTIGET
```

#### `F40D` DICTIGETREF

<p>Looks up key represented by a signed (big-endian) <code>n</code>-bit <em>Integer</em> <code>i</code> in dictionary <code>D</code> of type <code>HashmapE(n,^Y)</code>. On success, applies <code>LDREF</code> <code>ENDS</code> to the found value, returning a <em>Cell</em> <code>c</code> instead of a <em>Slice</em>. If <code>i</code> does not fit into <code>n</code> bits or the key is absent, returns <em>Null</em>.</p><br />
**Category:** Dict Get (dict_get)<br />

```fift Fift
DICTIGETREF
```

#### `F40E` DICTUGET

<p>Looks up key represented by an unsigned (big-endian) <code>n</code>-bit <em>Integer</em> <code>i</code> in dictionary <code>D</code> of type <code>HashmapE(n,X)</code> with <code>n</code>-bit keys. On success, returns the found value as a <em>Slice</em> <code>x</code>. If <code>i</code> does not fit into <code>n</code> bits, returns <code>0</code>.</p><br />
**Category:** Dict Get (dict_get)<br />

```fift Fift
DICTUGET
```

#### `F459` DICTDEL

<p>Deletes <code>n</code>-bit key, represented by a <em>Slice</em> <code>k</code>, from dictionary <code>D</code>. ```fift Fift
DICTDEL
```

#### `F45A` DICTIDEL

**Category:** Dict Delete (dict_delete)<br />

```fift Fift

If <code>i</code> does not fit into <code>n</code> bits, simply returns <code>D</code> <code>0</code> (&quot;key not found, dictionary unmodified&quot;).</p><br />

If the key is present, returns the modified dictionary <code>D&#x27;</code>, applies <code>LDREF</code> <code>ENDS</code> to the original value associated with the key <code>k</code> so that the value returned <code>c</code> is a <em>Cell</em>, and returns the success flag <code>-1</code>. Otherwise, returns the original dictionary <code>D</code> and <code>0</code>.</p><br />
**Category:** Dict Delete (dict_delete)<br />

#### `F469` DICTGETOPTREF

<p>Looks up key <code>k</code> (represented by a <em>Slice</em>) in dictionary <code>D</code> of type <code>HashmapE(n,^Y)</code>. If the key is absent, returns <em>Null</em> instead of throwing an exception.</p><br />
**Category:** Dict Mayberef (dict_mayberef)<br />

```fift Fift
DICTGETOPTREF
```

Otherwise, returns the found value as a <em>Cell</em> <code>c</code>.</p><br />

DICTIGETOPTREF

#### `F4A0` DICTIGETJMP

<p>Looks up key represented by a signed (big-endian) <code>n</code>-bit <em>Integer</em> <code>i</code> in dictionary <code>D</code>. On success, <code>BLESS</code>es the found value into a continuation and transfers control to it as if by a <code>JMPX</code>. On failure, does nothing. This is useful for implementing <code>switch</code>/<code>case</code> constructions.</p><br />
**Category:** Dict Special (dict_special)<br />

```fift Fift
DICTIGETJMP
```

#### `F4A1` DICTUGETJMP

<p>Looks up key represented by an unsigned (big-endian) <code>n</code>-bit <em>Integer</em> <code>i</code> in dictionary <code>D</code>. On success, <code>BLESS</code>es the found value into a continuation and transfers control to it as if by a <code>JMPX</code>. On failure, does nothing. ```fift Fift
DICTUGETJMP
```

#### `F4A2` DICTIGETEXEC

<p>Looks up key represented by a signed (big-endian) <code>n</code>-bit <em>Integer</em> <code>i</code> in dictionary <code>D</code>. On success, <code>BLESS</code>es the found value into a continuation and executes it as if by <code>EXECUTE</code>. On failure, does nothing. #### `F4A6_n` DICTPUSHCONST

<p>The dictionary itself is created from the first of remaining references of the current continuation. In this way, the complete <code>DICTPUSHCONST</code> instruction can be obtained by first serializing <code>xF4A4&#95;</code>, then the non-empty dictionary itself (one <code>1</code> bit and a <code>Cell</code> reference), and then the unsigned 10-bit integer <code>key&#95;len</code> (as if by a <code>STU 10</code> instruction).</p><br />
**Category:** Dict Special (dict_special)<br />

```fift Fift
[ref] [n] DICTPUSHCONST
```

#### `F4A8` PFXDICTGETQ

<p>Looks up the unique prefix of <em>Slice</em> <code>s</code> present in the prefix code dictionary represented by <code>Cell^?</code> <code>D</code> and <code>n</code>. If found, the prefix of <code>s</code> is returned as <code>s&#x27;</code>, and the corresponding value (also a <em>Slice</em>) as <code>x</code>. The remainder of <code>s</code> is returned as a <em>Slice</em> <code>s&#x27;&#x27;</code>. If no prefix of <code>s</code> is a key in prefix code dictionary <code>D</code>, returns the unchanged <code>s</code> and a zero flag to indicate failure.</p><br />
**Category:** Dict Special (dict_special)<br />

```fift Fift
PFXDICTGETQ
```

#### `F4A9` PFXDICTGET

<p>Looks up the unique prefix of <em>Slice</em> <code>s</code> present in the prefix code dictionary represented by <code>Cell^?</code> <code>D</code> and <code>n</code>. If found, the prefix of <code>s</code> is returned as <code>s&#x27;</code>, and the corresponding value (also a <em>Slice</em>) as <code>x</code>. The remainder of <code>s</code> is returned as a <em>Slice</em> <code>s&#x27;&#x27;</code>. If no prefix of <code>s</code> is a key in prefix code dictionary <code>D</code>, throws a <code>Cell</code> deserialization failure exception.</p><br />
**Category:** Dict Special (dict_special)<br />

```fift Fift
PFXDICTGET
```

#### `F4AA` PFXDICTGETJMP

<p>Looks up the unique prefix of <em>Slice</em> <code>s</code> present in the prefix code dictionary represented by <code>Cell^?</code> <code>D</code> and <code>n</code>. If found, <code>BLESS</code>es the corresponding value into a <em>Continuation</em> and transfers control to it as if by a <code>JMPX</code>. If no prefix of <code>s</code> is a key in prefix code dictionary <code>D</code>, returns the unchanged <code>s</code> and continues execution.</p><br />
**Category:** Dict Special (dict_special)<br />

```fift Fift
PFXDICTGETJMP
```

#### `F4AB` PFXDICTGETEXEC

<p>Looks up the unique prefix of <em>Slice</em> <code>s</code> present in the prefix code dictionary represented by <code>Cell^?</code> <code>D</code> and <code>n</code>. If found, <code>BLESS</code>es the corresponding value into a <em>Continuation</em> and executes it as if by <code>EXECUTE</code>. If no prefix of <code>s</code> is a key in prefix code dictionary <code>D</code>, throws a <code>Cell</code> deserialization exception.</p><br />
**Category:** Dict Special (dict_special)<br />

```fift Fift
PFXDICTGETEXEC
```

#### `F4AE_n` PFXDICTCONSTGETJMP

<p>Looks up a <code>prefix</code> in dictionary <code>D</code> and if found, jumps to the corresponding continuation. Similar to <code>PFXDICTGETJMP</code> but with predefined dictionary and key length.</p><br />
**Category:** Dict Special (dict_special)<br />

```fift Fift
[ref] [n] PFXDICTCONSTGETJMP
[ref] [n] PFXDICTSWITCH
```


<p><strong>Aliases</strong>:</p>
<ul>
<li>
<p><code>PFXDICTSWITCH</code></p>
<p>Current TxTracer name for <code>PFXDICTCONSTGETJMP</code>.</p>
</li>
</ul>

#### `F4BC` DICTIGETJMPZ

<p>Looks up key represented by a signed (big-endian) <code>n</code>-bit <em>Integer</em> <code>i</code> in dictionary <code>D</code>. On success, <code>BLESS</code>es the found value into a continuation and transfers control to it as if by a <code>JMPX</code>. On failure, returns the index <code>i</code> and continues execution. #### `F4B1` SUBDICTGET

<p>Constructs a subdictionary consisting of all keys beginning with prefix <code>k</code> (represented by a <em>Slice</em>, the first data bits of which are used as a key) of length <code>l</code> in dictionary <code>D</code> of type <code>HashmapE(n,X)</code> with <code>n</code>-bit keys. #### `F800` ACCEPT

<p>Sets current gas limit <code>g&#95;l</code> to its maximal allowed value <code>g&#95;m</code>, and resets the gas credit <code>g&#95;c</code> to zero, decreasing the value of <code>g&#95;r</code> by <code>g&#95;c</code> in the process.
In other words, the current smart contract agrees to buy some gas to finish the current transaction. This action is required to process external messages, which bring no value (hence no gas) with themselves.</p><br />
**Category:** App Gas (app_gas)<br />

```fift Fift
ACCEPT
```

#### `F801` SETGASLIMIT

<p>Sets current gas limit <code>g&#95;l</code> to the minimum of <code>g</code> and <code>g&#95;m</code>, and resets the gas credit <code>g&#95;c</code> to zero. If the gas consumed so far (including the present instruction) exceeds the resulting value of <code>g&#95;l</code>, an (unhandled) out of gas exception is thrown before setting new gas limits. Notice that <code>SETGASLIMIT</code> with an argument <code>g &gt;= 2^63-1</code> is equivalent to <code>ACCEPT</code>.</p><br />
**Category:** App Gas (app_gas)<br />

```fift Fift
SETGASLIMIT
```

#### `F807` GASCONSUMED

<p>Returns gas consumed by VM so far (including this instruction) in current Computation Phase.</p><br />
**Category:** App Gas (app_gas)<br />

```fift Fift
GASCONSUMED
```

#### `F80F` COMMIT

<p>Commits the current state of registers <code>c4</code> (&#x27;persistent data&#x27;) and <code>c5</code> (&#x27;actions&#x27;) so that the current execution is considered &#x27;successful&#x27; with the saved values even if an exception is thrown later.</p><br />
**Category:** App Gas (app_gas)<br />

```fift Fift
COMMIT
```

#### `F810` RANDU256

<p>Generates a new pseudo-random unsigned 256-bit <em>Integer</em> <code>x</code>. The algorithm is as follows: if <code>r</code> is the old value of the random seed, considered as a 32-byte array (by constructing the big-endian representation of an unsigned 256-bit integer), then its <code>sha512(r)</code> is computed; the first 32 bytes of this hash are stored as the new value <code>r&#x27;</code> of the random seed, and the remaining 32 bytes are returned as the next random value <code>x</code>.</p><br />
**Category:** App Rnd (app_rnd)<br />

```fift Fift
RANDU256
```

#### `F811` RAND

<p>Generates a new pseudo-random integer <code>z</code> in the range <code>0...y-1</code> (or <code>y...-1</code>, if <code>y&lt;0</code>). More precisely, an unsigned random value <code>x</code> is generated as in <code>RAND256U</code>; then <code>z:=floor(x&#42;y/2^256)</code> is computed.</p><br />
**Category:** App Rnd (app_rnd)<br />

```fift Fift
RAND
```

#### `F814` SETRAND

<p>Sets the random seed to unsigned 256-bit <em>Integer</em> <code>x</code>.</p><br />
**Category:** App Rnd (app_rnd)<br />

```fift Fift
SETRAND
```

#### `F815` ADDRAND

<p>Mixes unsigned 256-bit <em>Integer</em> <code>x</code> into the random seed <code>r</code> by setting the random seed to <code>Sha</code> of the concatenation of two 32-byte strings: the first with the big-endian representation of the old seed <code>r</code>, and the second with the big-endian representation of <code>x</code>.</p><br />
**Category:** App Rnd (app_rnd)<br />

```fift Fift
ADDRAND
RANDOMIZE
```

#### `F82i` GETPARAM

<p>Returns the <code>i</code>-th parameter from the <em>Tuple</em> provided at <code>c7</code>.</p><br />
**Category:** App Config (app_config)<br />

```fift Fift
[i] GETPARAM
```


<p><strong>Aliases</strong>:</p>
<ul>
<li>
<p><code>NOW</code></p>
<p>Returns the current Unix time as an <em>Integer</em>. If it is impossible to recover the requested value starting from <code>c7</code>, throws a type checking or range checking exception as appropriate.
Equivalent to <code>3 GETPARAM</code>.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p><code>BLOCKLT</code></p>
<p>Returns the starting logical time of the current block.
Equivalent to <code>4 GETPARAM</code>.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p><code>LTIME</code></p>
<p>Returns the logical time of the current transaction.
Equivalent to <code>5 GETPARAM</code>.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p><code>RANDSEED</code></p>
<p>Returns the current random seed as an unsigned 256-bit <em>Integer</em>.
Equivalent to <code>6 GETPARAM</code>.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p><code>BALANCE</code></p>
<p>Returns the remaining balance of the smart contract as a <em>Tuple</em> consisting of an <em>Integer</em> (the remaining Gram balance in nanograms) and a <em>Maybe Cell</em> (a dictionary with 32-bit keys representing the balance of &#x27;&#x27;extra currencies&#x27;&#x27;).
Equivalent to <code>7 GETPARAM</code>.
Note that <code>RAW</code> primitives such as <code>SENDRAWMSG</code> do not update this field.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p><code>MYADDR</code></p>
<p>Returns the internal address of the current smart contract as a <em>Slice</em> with a <code>MsgAddressInt</code>. If necessary, it can be parsed further using primitives such as <code>PARSEMSGADDR</code> or <code>REWRITESTDADDR</code>.
Equivalent to <code>8 GETPARAM</code>.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p><code>CONFIGROOT</code></p>
<p>Returns the <em>Maybe Cell</em> <code>D</code> with the current global configuration dictionary. Equivalent to <code>9 GETPARAM </code>.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p><code>MYCODE</code></p>
<p>Retrieves code of smart-contract from c7. Equivalent to <code>10 GETPARAM </code>.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p><code>INCOMINGVALUE</code></p>
<p>Retrieves value of incoming message from c7. Equivalent to <code>11 GETPARAM </code>.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p><code>STORAGEFEES</code></p>
<p>Retrieves value of storage phase fees from c7. Equivalent to <code>12 GETPARAM </code>.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p><code>PREVBLOCKSINFOTUPLE</code></p>
<p>Retrives PrevBlocksInfo: <code>[last&#95;mc&#95;blocks, prev&#95;key&#95;block]</code> from c7. Equivalent to <code>13 GETPARAM </code>.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p><code>UNPACKEDCONFIGTUPLE</code></p>
<p>Retrives tuple that contains some config parameters as cell slices. If the parameter is absent from the config, the value is null. Values:</p>
<ul>
<li>
<p><strong>0</strong>: <code>StoragePrices</code> from <code>ConfigParam 18</code>. Not the whole dict, but only the one StoragePrices entry (one which corresponds to the current time).</p>
<ul>
<li><strong>1</strong>: <code>ConfigParam 19</code> (global id).</li>
<li><strong>2</strong>: <code>ConfigParam 20</code> (mc gas prices).</li>
<li><strong>3</strong>: <code>ConfigParam 21</code> (gas prices).</li>
<li><strong>4</strong>: <code>ConfigParam 24</code> (mc fwd fees).</li>
<li><strong>5</strong>: <code>ConfigParam 25</code> (fwd fees).</li>
<li><strong>6</strong>: <code>ConfigParam 43</code> (size limits).</li>
</ul>
</li>
</ul>
</li>
<li>
<p><code>DUEPAYMENT</code></p>
<p>Retrives current debt for storage fee (nanotons).</p>
</li>
</ul>

GETPRECOMPILEDGAS
```

#### `F83A` GETORIGINALFWDFEE

<p>Calculate <code>fwd&#95;fee &#42; 2^16 / first&#95;frac</code>. Can be used to get the original <code>fwd&#95;fee</code> of the message.</p><br />
**Category:** App Config (app_config)<br />

```fift Fift
GETORIGINALFWDFEE
```

#### `F83B` GETGASFEESIMPLE

<p>Same as <code>GETGASFEE</code>, but without flat price (just <code>(gas&#95;used &#42; price) / 2^16)</code>.</p><br />
**Category:** App Config (app_config)<br />

```fift Fift
GETGASFEESIMPLE
```

#### `F83C` GETFORWARDFEESIMPLE

<p>Same as <code>GETFORWARDFEE</code>, but without lump price (just (<code>bits&#42;bit&#95;price + cells&#42;cell&#95;price) / 2^16</code>).</p><br />
**Category:** App Config (app_config)<br />

```fift Fift
GETFORWARDFEESIMPLE
```

#### `F880` GETEXTRABALANCE

<p>Takes id of the extra currency (integer in range <code>0..2^32-1</code>), returns the amount of this extra currency on the account balance. The first <code>5</code> executions of <code>GETEXTRABALANCE</code> consume at most <code>26 + 200</code> gas each. The subsequent executions incur the full gas cost of <code>26</code> (normal instruction cost) plus gas for loading cells (up to <code>3300</code> if the dictionary has maximum depth).</p><br />
**Category:** App Global (app_global)<br />

```fift Fift
GETEXTRABALANCE
```

#### `F881ii` GETPARAMLONG

**Category:** App Config (app_config)<br />

```fift Fift
[i] GETPARAMLONG
```

#### `F89i` INMSGPARAM

<p>Returns a specific parameter from the inbound message parameters tuple.</p><br />
**Category:** App Config (app_config)<br />

```fift Fift
[i] INMSGPARAM
```


<p><strong>Aliases</strong>:</p>
<ul>
<li>
<p><code>INMSG_BOUNCE</code></p>
<p>Retrives <code>bounce</code> flag of incoming message.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p><code>INMSG_BOUNCED</code></p>
<p>Retrives <code>bounced</code> flag of incoming message.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p><code>INMSG_SRC</code></p>
<p>Retrives <code>src</code> flag of incoming message.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p><code>INMSG_FWDFEE</code></p>
<p>Retrives <code>fwd&#95;fee</code> field of incoming message.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p><code>INMSG_LT</code></p>
<p>Retrives <code>lt</code> field of incoming message.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p><code>INMSG_UTIME</code></p>
<p>Retrives <code>utime</code> field of incoming message.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p><code>INMSG_ORIGVALUE</code></p>
<p>Retrives original value of the message. This is sometimes different from the value in <code>INCOMINGVALUE</code> and TVM stack because of storage fees.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p><code>INMSG_VALUE</code></p>
<p>Retrives value of the message after deducting storage fees. This is same as in <code>INCOMINGVALUE</code> and TVM stack.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p><code>INMSG_VALUEEXTRA</code></p>
<p>Same as in <code>INCOMINGVALUE</code>.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p><code>INMSG_STATEINIT</code></p>
<p>Retrieves <code>init</code> field of the incoming message.</p>
</li>
</ul>

#### `F900` HASHCU

<p>Computes the representation hash of a <em>Cell</em> <code>c</code> and returns it as a 256-bit unsigned integer <code>hash</code>. Useful for signing and checking signatures of arbitrary entities represented by a tree of cells.</p><br />
**Category:** App Crypto (app_crypto)<br />

```fift Fift
HASHCU
```

#### `F901` HASHSU

<p>Computes the hash of a <em>Slice</em> <code>s</code> and returns it as a 256-bit unsigned integer <code>hash</code>. The result is the same as if an ordinary cell containing only data and references from <code>s</code> had been created and its hash computed by <code>HASHCU</code>.</p><br />
**Category:** App Crypto (app_crypto)<br />

```fift Fift
HASHSU
```

#### `F902` SHA256U

<p>Computes <code>Sha</code> of the data bits of <em>Slice</em> <code>s</code>. If the bit length of <code>s</code> is not divisible by eight, throws a cell underflow exception. The hash value is returned as a 256-bit unsigned integer <code>hash</code>.</p><br />
**Category:** App Crypto (app_crypto)<br />

```fift Fift
SHA256U
```

#### `F90400` HASHEXT_SHA256

<p>Calculates and returns hash of the concatenation of slices or builders <code>s&#95;1</code>...<code>s&#95;length</code>.</p>
<p>Hash ID can be one of the following:</p>
<ul>
<li><code>0</code> - <strong>SHA256</strong> (1/33 gas per byte)</li>
<li><code>1</code> - <strong>SHA512</strong> (1/16 gas per byte)</li>
<li><code>2</code> - <strong>BLAKE2B</strong> (1/19 gas per byte)</li>
<li><code>3</code> - <strong>KECCAK256</strong> (1/11 gas per byte)</li>
<li><code>4</code> - <strong>KECCAK512</strong> (1/6 gas per byte)</li>

**Category:** App Crypto (app_crypto)<br />

#### `F90603` HASHEXTA_KECCAK256

<li><code>3</code> - <strong>KECCAK256</strong> (1/11 gas per byte)</li>

#### `F910` CHKSIGNU

<p>Checks the Ed25519-signature <code>s</code> of a hash <code>h</code> (a 256-bit unsigned integer, usually computed as the hash of some data) using public key <code>k</code> (also represented by a 256-bit unsigned integer).
The signature <code>s</code> must be a <em>Slice</em> containing at least 512 data bits; only the first 512 bits are used. The result is <code>-1</code> if the signature is valid, <code>0</code> otherwise.
Notice that <code>CHKSIGNU</code> is equivalent to <code>ROT</code> <code>NEWC</code> <code>256 STU</code> <code>ENDC</code> <code>ROTREV</code> <code>CHKSIGNS</code>, i.e., to <code>CHKSIGNS</code> with the first argument <code>d</code> set to 256-bit <em>Slice</em> containing <code>h</code>. Therefore, if <code>h</code> is computed as the hash of some data, these data are hashed <em>twice</em>, the second hashing occurring inside <code>CHKSIGNS</code>.</p><br />
**Category:** App Crypto (app_crypto)<br />

```fift Fift
CHKSIGNU
```

#### `F911` CHKSIGNS

<p>Checks whether <code>s</code> is a valid Ed25519-signature of the data portion of <em>Slice</em> <code>d</code> using public key <code>k</code>, similarly to <code>CHKSIGNU</code>. If the bit length of <em>Slice</em> <code>d</code> is not divisible by eight, throws a cell underflow exception. The verification of Ed25519 signatures is the standard one, with <code>Sha</code> used to reduce <code>d</code> to the 256-bit number that is actually signed.</p><br />
**Category:** App Crypto (app_crypto)<br />

```fift Fift
CHKSIGNS
```

#### `F912` ECRECOVER

<p>Recovers public key from signature, identical to Bitcoin/Ethereum operations. Takes 32-byte hash as uint256 <code>hash</code>; 65-byte signature as uint8 <code>v</code> and uint256 <code>r</code>, <code>s</code>. Returns <code>0</code> on failure, public key and <code>-1</code> on success. 65-byte public key is returned as uint8 <code>h</code>, uint256 <code>x1</code>, <code>x2</code>.</p><br />
**Category:** App Crypto (app_crypto)<br />

```fift Fift
ECRECOVER
```

#### `F913` SECP256K1_XONLY_PUBKEY_TWEAK_ADD

<p><code>key</code> and <code>tweak</code> are 256-bit unsigned integers. 65-byte public key is returned as <code>uint8 f</code>, <code>uint256 x, y</code> as in <code>ECRECOVER</code>.</p><br />
**Category:** App Crypto (app_crypto)<br />

```fift Fift
SECP256K1_XONLY_PUBKEY_TWEAK_ADD
```

#### `F914` P256_CHKSIGNU

<p>Checks seck256r1-signature <code>sig</code> of a number <code>h</code> (a 256-bit unsigned integer, usually computed as the hash of some data) and public key <code>k</code>. Returns -1 on success, 0 on failure. Public key is a 33-byte slice (encoded according to Sec. 2.3.4 point 2 of <a href="https://www.secg.org/sec1-v2.pdf">SECG SEC 1</a>). Signature <code>sig</code> is a 64-byte slice (two 256-bit unsigned integers <code>r</code> and <code>s</code>).</p><br />
**Category:** App Crypto (app_crypto)<br />

```fift Fift
P256_CHKSIGNU
```

Public key is a 33-byte slice (encoded according to Sec. 2.3.4 point 2 of <a href="https://www.secg.org/sec1-v2.pdf">SECG SEC 1</a>). #### `F940` CDATASIZEQ

<p>Recursively computes the count of distinct cells <code>x</code>, data bits <code>y</code>, and cell references <code>z</code> in the dag rooted at <em>Cell</em> <code>c</code>, effectively returning the total storage used by this dag taking into account the identification of equal cells. The values of <code>x</code>, <code>y</code>, and <code>z</code> are computed by a depth-first traversal of this dag, with a hash table of visited cell hashes used to prevent visits of already-visited cells. The total count of visited cells <code>x</code> cannot exceed non-negative <em>Integer</em> <code>n</code>; otherwise the computation is aborted before visiting the <code>(n+1)</code>-st cell and a zero is returned to indicate failure. If <code>c</code> is <em>Null</em>, returns <code>x=y=z=0</code>.</p><br />
**Category:** App Misc (app_misc)<br />

```fift Fift
CDATASIZEQ
```

#### `F941` CDATASIZE

<p>A non-quiet version of <code>CDATASIZEQ</code> that throws a cell overflow exception (8) on failure.</p><br />
**Category:** App Misc (app_misc)<br />

```fift Fift
CDATASIZE
```

#### `F942` SDATASIZEQ

<p>Recursively computes the count of distinct cells <code>x</code>, data bits <code>y</code>, and cell references <code>z</code> in the dag rooted at <em>Slice</em> <code>s</code>, effectively returning the total storage used by this dag taking into account the identification of equal cells. The values of <code>x</code>, <code>y</code>, and <code>z</code> are computed by a depth-first traversal of this dag, with a hash table of visited cell hashes used to prevent visits of already-visited cells. The total count of visited cells <code>x</code> cannot exceed non-negative <em>Integer</em> <code>n</code>; otherwise the computation is aborted before visiting the <code>(n+1)</code>-st cell and a zero is returned to indicate failure. The returned value of <code>x</code> does not take into account the cell that contains the slice <code>s</code> itself; however, the data bits and the cell references of <code>s</code> are accounted for in <code>y</code> and <code>z</code>.</p><br />
**Category:** App Misc (app_misc)<br />

```fift Fift
SDATASIZEQ
```

#### `F943` SDATASIZE

<p>A non-quiet version of <code>SDATASIZEQ</code> that throws a cell overflow exception (8) on failure.</p><br />
**Category:** App Misc (app_misc)<br />

```fift Fift
SDATASIZE
```

#### `FA00` LDGRAMS

<p>Loads a <code>Gram</code> or <code>VarUInteger 16</code> amount from <em>Slice</em> <code>s</code>, and returns the amount as <em>Integer</em> <code>x</code> along with the remainder <code>s&#x27;</code> of <code>s</code>. The expected serialization of <code>x</code> consists of a 4-bit unsigned big-endian integer <code>l</code>, followed by an <code>8l</code>-bit unsigned big-endian representation of <code>x</code>.</p><br />
**Category:** App Currency (app_currency)<br />

```fift Fift
LDGRAMS
LDVARUINT16
```


<p><strong>Aliases</strong>:</p>
<ul>
<li><code>LDVARUINT16</code></li>
</ul>

#### `FA01` LDVARINT16

<p>Loads a <code>VarInteger 16</code> amount from <em>Slice</em> <code>s</code>, and returns the amount as <em>Integer</em> <code>x</code> along with the remainder <code>s&#x27;</code> of <code>s</code>. The expected serialization of <code>x</code> consists of a 4-bit unsigned big-endian integer <code>l</code>, followed by an <code>8l</code>-bit signed big-endian representation of <code>x</code>.</p><br />
**Category:** App Currency (app_currency)<br />

```fift Fift
LDVARINT16
```

#### `FA02` STGRAMS

<p>Stores an integer <code>x</code> in the range <code>0...2^120-1</code> into <em>Builder</em> <code>b</code>, and returns the resulting <em>Builder</em> <code>b&#x27;</code>. The serialization of <code>x</code> consists of a 4-bit unsigned big-endian integer <code>l</code>, which is the smallest integer <code>l&gt;=0</code>, such that <code>x&lt;2^(8l)</code>, followed by an <code>8l</code>-bit unsigned big-endian representation of <code>x</code>.</p><br />
**Category:** App Currency (app_currency)<br />

```fift Fift

```

#### `FA03` STVARINT16

<p>Stores a <em>signed</em> <em>Integer</em> <code>x</code> in the range <code>-2^119...2^119-1</code> into <em>Builder</em> <code>b</code>, and returns the resulting <em>Builder</em> <code>b&#x27;</code>. The serialization of <code>x</code> consists of a 4-bit unsigned big-endian integer <code>l</code>, which is the smallest integer <code>l&gt;=0</code>, such that <code>-2^(8l-1) &lt;= x &lt; 2^(8l-1)</code>, followed by an <code>8l</code>-bit signed big-endian representation of <code>x</code>.</p><br />
**Category:** App Currency (app_currency)<br />

```fift Fift
STVARINT16
```

#### `FA04` LDVARUINT32

The expected serialization of <code>x</code> consists of a 5-bit unsigned big-endian integer <code>l</code>, followed by an <code>8l</code>-bit unsigned big-endian representation of <code>x</code>.</p><br />
**Category:** App Currency (app_currency)<br />

```fift Fift
LDVARUINT32

#### `FA44` REWRITESTDADDR

#### `FA50` LDOPTSTDADDR

#### `FA51` LDOPTSTDADDRQ

If the address has any other tag, pushes a status flag 0. This is a quiet version of <code>LDOPTSTDADDR</code> which means that instead of throwing an exception, it pushes a status flag to the stack: 0 if the operation fails, -1 if the operation succeeds.</p><br />

#### `FB00` SENDRAWMSG

<p>Cell <code>msg</code> should contain a correctly serialized object <code>Message X</code>.</p>
<p>Source address can have dummy value <code>addr&#95;none</code>, and will be automatically replaced with the current smart-contract address.</p>
<p><code>ihr&#95;fee</code>, <code>fwd&#95;fee</code>, <code>created&#95;lt</code> and <code>created&#95;at</code> fields can also have arbitrary values and will be rewritten with correct values during the action phase of the current transaction.</p>
<p>Integer parameter <code>mode</code> contains the flags.</p>
<ul>
<li>
<p><code>mode=0</code> is used for ordinary messages.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p><code>mode=128</code> is used for messages that are to carry all the remaining balance of the current smart contract (instead of the value originally indicated in the message).</p>
</li>
<li>
<p><code>mode=64</code> is used for messages that carry all the remaining value of the inbound message in addition to the value initially indicated in the new message (if bit 0 is not set, the gas fees are deducted from this amount).</p>
</li>
<li>
<p><code>mode&#x27;=mode+1</code> means that the sender wants to pay transfer fees separately.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p><code>mode&#x27;=mode+2</code> means that any errors arising while processing this message during the action phase should be ignored.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p><code>mode&#x27;=mode+32</code> means that the current account must be destroyed if its resulting balance is zero. This flag is usually employed together with <code>+128</code>.</p>
</li>
</ul><br />
**Category:** App Actions (app_actions)<br />

```fift Fift
SENDRAWMSG
```

#### `FB02` RAWRESERVE

<p>This behavior is roughly equivalent to creating an outbound message carrying <code>amount</code> nanotons (or <code>b-amount</code> nanotons, where <code>b</code> is the remaining balance) to oneself, so that the subsequent output actions would not be able to spend more money than the remainder.</p>
<ul>
<li>
<p>Bit <code>+2</code> in <code>mode</code> means that the external action does not fail if the specified amount cannot be reserved; instead, all remaining balance is reserved.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Bit <code>+8</code> in <code>mode</code> means <code>amount=-amount</code> before performing any further actions.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Bit <code>+4</code> in <code>mode</code> means that <code>amount</code> is increased by the original balance of the current account (before the compute phase), including all extra currencies, before performing any other checks and actions.</p>
</li>
</ul><br />
**Category:** App Actions (app_actions)<br />

```fift Fift
RAWRESERVE
```

#### `FB03` RAWRESERVEX

<p>Similar to <code>RAWRESERVE</code>, but also accepts a dictionary <code>D</code> with extra currencies. In this way currencies other than TON can be reserved.</p><br />
**Category:** App Actions (app_actions)<br />

```fift Fift
RAWRESERVEX
```

#### `FB04` SETCODE

<p>Creates an output action that would change this smart contract code to that given by <em>Cell</em> <code>code</code>. This change will take effect only after the successful termination of the current run of the smart contract.</p><br />
**Category:** App Actions (app_actions)<br />

```fift Fift
SETCODE
```

#### `FB06` SETLIBCODE

<ul>
<li>
<p>If <code>mode=0</code>, the library is removed if it was previously present in the collection, if not, this action does nothing.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>If <code>mode=1</code>, the library is added as a private library.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>If <code>mode=2</code>, the library is added as a public library and becomes available to all smart contracts if the current smart contract resides in the masterchain.</p>
</li>
</ul>
<p>If the library was present in the collection before, its public/private status is changed according to <code>mode</code>. Values of <code>mode</code> other than <code>0...2</code> are invalid.</p><br />
**Category:** App Actions (app_actions)<br />

```fift Fift
SETLIBCODE
```

#### `FB07` CHANGELIB

<p>Creates an output action similarly to <code>SETLIBCODE</code>, but instead of the library code accepts its hash as an unsigned 256-bit integer <code>hash</code>. If <code>mode != 0</code> and the library with <code>hash</code> is absent from the library collection of this smart contract, this output action will fail.</p><br />
**Category:** App Actions (app_actions)<br />

```fift Fift
CHANGELIB
```

#### `FB08` SENDMSG

<p>Mode has the same effect as in the case of <code>SENDRAWMSG</code>.</p>
<p>Additionally <code>+1024</code> means — do not create an action, only estimate fee. Other modes affect the fee calculation as follows:</p>
<ul>
<li>
<p><code>+64</code> substitutes the entire balance of the incoming message as an outcoming value (slightly inaccurate, gas expenses that cannot be estimated before the computation is completed are not taken into account).</p>
</li>
<li>
<p><code>+128</code> substitutes the value of the entire balance of the contract before the start of the computation phase (slightly inaccurate, since gas expenses that cannot be estimated before the completion of the computation phase are not taken into account).</p>
</li>
</ul><br />
**Category:** App Actions (app_actions)<br />

```fift Fift
SENDMSG
```

#### `FEij` DEBUG

<ul>
<li>
<p>With <code>i=0</code> and <code>j=0</code> this instruction outputs the entire stack as <code>DUMPSTK</code>.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>With <code>i=1</code> and <code>j=4</code> this instruction outputs the string taken from the top of the stack as <code>STRDUMP</code>.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>With <code>i=2</code> and any <code>j</code> this instruction dumps a slice with length divisible by 8 from <code>j</code>-th element of the stack as a string as <code>DUMP</code>.</p>
</li>
</ul><br />
**Category:** Debug (debug)<br />

```fift Fift
{i*16+j} DEBUG
```


<p><strong>Aliases</strong>:</p>
<ul>
<li>
<p><code>DUMPSTK</code></p>
<p>Dumps the stack (at most the top 255 values) and shows the total stack depth. Does nothing on production versions of TVM.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p><code>STRDUMP</code></p>
<p>Dumps slice with length divisible by 8 from top of stack as a string. Does nothing on production versions of TVM.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p><code>DUMP</code></p>
<p>Dumps slice with length divisible by 8 from top of stack as a string. Does nothing on production versions of TVM.</p>
</li>
</ul>

#### `FEFnssss` DEBUGSTR

<p>Outputs passed string to debug logs.</p><br />
**Category:** Debug (debug)<br />

```fift Fift
{string} DEBUGSTR
{string} {x} DEBUGSTRI
```

<ul>
<li><code>DUMPTOSFMT</code></li>
<li><code>LOGSTR</code></li>
<li><code>PRINTSTR</code></li>
</ul>

#### `FFnn` SETCP

<p>Selects TVM codepage <code>0 &lt;= num &lt; 240</code>. If the codepage is not supported, throws an invalid opcode exception.</p><br />
**Category:** Codepage (codepage)<br />

```fift Fift
[nn] SETCP
```


<p><strong>Aliases</strong>:</p>
<ul>
<li>
<p><code>SETCP0</code></p>
<p>Selects TVM (test) codepage zero as described in this document.</p>
</li>
</ul>

#### `FFFz` SETCP_SPECIAL

<p>Selects TVM codepage <code>z-16</code> for <code>1 &lt;= z &lt;= 15</code>. Negative codepages <code>-13...-1</code> are reserved for restricted versions of TVM needed to validate runs of TVM in other codepages. Negative codepage <code>-14</code> is reserved for experimental codepages, not necessarily compatible between different TVM implementations, and should be disabled in the production versions of TVM.</p><br />
**Category:** Codepage (codepage)<br />

```fift Fift
[z-16] SETCP
```

#### `FFF0` SETCPX

<p>Selects codepage <code>num</code> with <code>num</code> from the top of the stack. If the codepage is not supported, throws an invalid opcode exception.</p><br />
**Category:** Codepage (codepage)<br />

```fift Fift
SETCPX
```

#### `B7B602` QBITSIZE

```fift Fift

```

```fift Fift

QEQINT
```

#### `B7C1` QLESSINT

<p>Compares integer from stack with argument for less than and returns <code>-1</code> if true and <code>0</code> otherwise. If the operand is <code>NaN</code>, returns <code>NaN</code> instead of throwing an exception.</p><br />
**Category:** Arithm Quiet (arithm_quiet)<br />

```fift Fift
QLESSINT
```

#### `B7C2` QGTINT

<p>Compares integer from stack with argument for greater than and returns <code>-1</code> if true and <code>0</code> otherwise. If the operand is <code>NaN</code>, returns <code>NaN</code> instead of throwing an exception.</p><br />
**Category:** Arithm Quiet (arithm_quiet)<br />

```fift Fift
QGTINT
```

#### `B7C3` QNEQINT

<p>Compares integer from stack with argument for inequality and returns <code>-1</code> if true and <code>0</code> otherwise. If the operand is <code>NaN</code>, returns <code>NaN</code> instead of throwing an exception.</p><br />
**Category:** Arithm Quiet (arithm_quiet)<br />

```fift Fift
QNEQINT
```

#### `DA` CALLXARGS_1

#### `FF` SETCP_SHORT

<p>Selects TVM codepage <code>num</code> for <code>-256 &lt;= num &lt;= -1</code>. Negative codepages <code>-13...-1</code> are reserved for restricted versions of TVM needed to validate runs of TVM in other codepages. Negative codepage <code>-14</code> is reserved for experimental codepages, not necessarily compatible between different TVM implementations, and should be disabled in the production versions of TVM.</p><br />
**Category:** Codepage (codepage)<br />

```fift Fift
SETCP_SHORT
```

#### `F88111` INMSGPARAMS

<p>Returns the 17th element of the c7 tuple, which contains inbound message parameters. The tuple includes: bounce (boolean), bounced (boolean), src_addr (slice), fwd_fee (int), created_lt (int), created_at (int), orig_value (int), value (int), value_extra (cell or null), state_init (cell or null). For external messages, tick-tock transactions and get methods: bounce, bounced, fwd_fee, created_lt, created_at, orig_value, value are 0, value_extra is null. For tick-tock transactions and get methods: src_addr is addr_none.</p><br />
**Category:** App Config (app_config)<br />

```fift Fift
INMSGPARAMS
```

#### `F881` GETPARAMLONG2

<p>Same as <code>i GETPARAM</code>, but <code>i</code> is in range <code>[0..254]</code>.</p><br />
**Category:** App Config (app_config)<br />

```fift Fift
GETPARAMLONG2
```
